This immediately reminds us that Moshe Rabbeinu’s birth, his rescue, and his upbringing are to be credited to two women, a mother and daughter: Yocheved, Moshe Rabbeinu’s mother, and Miriam, his sister. At the time when Pharaoh’s decrees reached their most critical moments and brought about despair and helplessness even in the leading Jewish families, these two women—one a mother and the other still a very young girl—continued with their work of *mesiras nefesh* to raise a new generation of Jews, the generation of the Geulah. In the most difficult times of the Egyptian exile, they not only inspired the other women but also the

## 218

men, and they merited that through them came the Redeemer, and the redemption, of the Jewish people from the Egyptian exile.

In our time, especially in the final generations of the current difficult exile, Jewish women, mothers and daughters, have the same task, and the same responsibility and *zechus*, as the Jewish women in the first exile. The Rebbe, my father-in-law, often emphasized this in word and in writing. In this current year, the 150th year since the *histalkus* of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of the Chabad *shita* and way of life, we must remember with special enthusiasm the great influence that Rebbetzin Rivkah had on the upbringing of her son, the Alter Rebbe, as it is described in the memoirs of the Rebbe, my father-in-law.

With a deep, inner hope, I hope that the students of "Beis Rivkah" will always remember and correctly appreciate their great responsibility and *zechus* in continuing the holy traditions of the Jewish woman, not only in their own homes, where the woman is the *akeres habayis*, the foundation of the home, but also through active involvement in the widest circles of women, in order to help raise a loyal Jewish generation that will merit the *Geulah Shleimah*, speedily in our days.

And with the same earnest hope, I hope that the *baalei batim*, *askanim*, and friends of "Beis Rivkah" will apply every effort—in time, money, and energy—to give the "Beis Rivkah" school the full possibility to expand and grow according to the demands of the current urgent time.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you all, in general and each one in particular, success in all the above-mentioned matters and in everything one needs, in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius* alike.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings.


## כ"ד טבת

219

24 Teves

I am writing to confirm receipt of your letter dated 7 Teves, along with the materials enclosed—reading sheets, booklets, and so on, regarding the Alter Rebbe, the founder of the Chabad movement—for the students of the schools.

It is surely superfluous to emphasize the immense value of the very matter of disseminating the fundamental values of Torah and Yiddishkeit, especially among the youth, as any positive influence upon them while they are young brings forth fruit and fruit of fruit throughout their entire lives. Therefore, there is no need for me to express thanks for the great deed you have performed, for the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself. However, I do owe you my thanks for your thoughtfulness and the effort you took to send me all the materials; thank you very much.

May it be the will of Hashem that you see good fruit from your labor in general, and from your labor in the aforementioned matter in particular. May the students of the various classes who read and study this material about the pride and glory of Israel—the personality and Torah of the Alter Rebbe—find that it is a study which leads to action, a conduct founded upon the love of Hashem, the love of Torah, and the love of Israel, permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, uniting the heart and the mind together.

Following the conversation we had, the memory of which is of course preserved with me, there is surely no need to elaborate on the great value of the points mentioned and their implications. We "bring about merit through a meritorious day," as today is the yahrtzeit-hilula of the Alter Rebbe.

In continuation of the above, I will take the liberty of enclosing a copy of a general letter for Rosh Hashanah in connection with the Shmittah year of this year. I would also like to draw your attention—though it has surely already been brought to your notice—that this year is the 100th anniversary of the passing of the grandson (and successor) of the Alter Rebbe, known by the name of his books as the Tzemach Tzedek.

With heartfelt thanks for the above, and with respect and blessing.
(From a letter, 24 Teves, 5726)

I was pleased to receive the telegram confirming receipt of the two books of the Alter Rebbe. For several reasons, this letter of mine was delayed until today, the day of his hilula.

Similar to what I wrote in my previous letter regarding physical construction—that no matter how much one estimates what is needed to invest in the building, when one comes to the actual work, one becomes impoverished and requires hidden powers, and even one's own inner powers—this is all the more so regarding spiritual construction, and as the expression...

223

...that is called *Chinuch Katan*, as well as in the text of the *Shaar HaTanya*, which I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: that the words "Sefer Likutei Amarim, etc., in a long and short way, with the help of Hashem," are the language of the Alter Rebbe, and in the *Pnei Melech* (in reverse order).

Incidentally, the aforementioned language is also found in *Avodas HaKodesh* by R. Meir ibn Gabbai, Part 4, Chapter 1, and in the *Shelah* in several places. [Found in one Chassidic manuscript: See Yerushalmi, Yevamos, Chapter 4, Halacha 11, "Rava d'masnisa, rava d'ulfana," see there.]
(From a letter, 11 Iyar, 5718)

...b) Thank you for pointing out the printing error you found in the *Moreh Shiur* for the day of 7 Shevat in a leap year. It is as I wrote in my previous letter: due to my many preoccupations, I entrusted and relied upon others for proofreading such things, and in general, the verse says, "Who can discern errors?"

c) Regarding your note on the *Tikkun Derech Efshar*, page 410, changing *Moreinu* to *Moreinu HaChassid*, and *Moreinu* to *HaChassid*: Because I found it recorded as such in the margins of a Tanya, and it was copied from the Tanya of the elder Chassidim of past generations—who, as is evident from his other notes, were reliable—I could not clearly ascertain who it was. Therefore, I placed his changes in the section of *Tikkunim* in *Derech Efshar*.

d) Regarding the doubt in Tanya, Chapter 1, page 5, line 7, in the word "mizeh" (from this): In my opinion, it continues to what precedes it. Similarly, the word "zeh" (this) on page 24b, line 11, although some say it continues to what follows below. This requires further study in the *Kuntres Bikkur Chicago*, page 63 and onwards...

z) Regarding what you write, that you possess a small manuscript commentary on the Tanya: The copy that is with... is not with me. However, I found here a *Biur Tanya* which, according to what is recorded on it, is from R. Hillel of Paritch, starting from *Likutei Amarim*, Chapter 1, etc., and although it is truly known that "the righteousness of the righteous and the wickedness of the wicked is in the thought, etc.," and it concludes with a commentary on Chapter 12—if this is not what you have, as you suggested, perhaps you could send it to me for a certain period of time...
(From a letter, 14 Adar I, 5714)

224

...Regarding what you noted concerning what is written in the *Tanya d'Bei Rav*: "The name 'tzaddik' is a gift from Above," and Rabba said, "I am a beinoni," because he occupied himself with Torah, and only one who occupies himself with Torah and acts of kindness has his inclination delivered into his hand (*Avodah Zarah* 5b). You wish to explain that "his inclination is delivered into his hand" refers to the aforementioned level of *tzaddik*. In my humble opinion, this cannot be said, for occupying oneself with Torah and acts of kindness is the duty of every single person and depends entirely on his own free choice, whereas the level of *tzaddik* is such that "a person does not have the power of choice in this to such an extent, etc." (*Tanya*, Chapter 14). See there that a person's effort in attaining this level is through *hisbonenus* (contemplation), etc., and not through occupying oneself with Torah and acts of kindness. It must be said that "their inclination is delivered" refers to the practical aspect in *machshava, dibbur, u'maaseh* (thought, speech, and action), as explained in Chapter 13, and not like the matter of "their heart is in their own control," which is explained in Chapter 15.
(From a letter, Yemei HaSelichos, 5719)

...Regarding the note on *Chinuch Katan* (in the Tanya): You are certainly correct that "train a youth, etc." and its explanation applies to every person. A verse does not depart from its literal meaning. On the contrary, the level of *beinonim* is the level of every person, and *tzaddikim* are few.

And what is written at the end of *Chinuch Katan*, "a *tzaddik* falls and rises, etc.," is to resolve the difficulty in the second half of that verse—that this training is a virtue for the youth even if he reaches the level of an elder (*tzaddik*), and even after he ages. [It is understood, and all the more so, regarding every person—that he is in need of the love with which he was trained, etc., from his youth.]

Regarding the order and study of Chabad Chassidus: It is the same as with the entire Torah. Order is necessary for a beginner (Mikra, then Mishnah, etc., and subsequently in the order of the yeshivos—including Tomchei Temimim), but afterwards—in addition to the general instruction of our Sages to study in the place (also in the spiritual sense) that his heart desires—the main thing is that it should be in abundance, in quality ("you have labored") and in quantity.

See *Bach* to *Tur Orach Chaim*, section 47, in the entry *Amar Rabbi Yochanan Amar Rabbi*. It is a great mitzvah, and now especially, to publicize it.
(From a letter, 12 Teves, 5742)

In response to your letter of 12 Iyar: What you wrote, that there is no one in your vicinity who can study—with the help of Heaven—the *maamarim* of *Torah Or* and *Likutei Torah*, is consistent with the *sicha* of Shabbos Mevarchim before Chanukah... already


## בא

## 226

### Bo

...In your letter, you write that there are 26 other Jewish bochurim with you who are currently still "free" (in the sense of Torah and mitzvos). You are certainly doing as much as you can to bring them closer to Torah and mitzvos so that they will actually fulfill them in practice. You must not be discouraged by the excuses they give you; on the contrary, this only shows how great the pity is for them. When you speak with them, you will eventually have an effect on them—a little at first, and later, more and more. 

Especially regarding putting on tefillin, you must explain to them that besides the fact that it is one of the mitzvos of Hashem Yisbarach, it is also a segulah for long life. Just as in the military, one learns how to conduct oneself to avoid harm, chas v’shalom, and one who does not learn this brings harm upon himself and also acts against the government—so too, every Jewish soldier has his means of protection, and one of them is putting on tefillin. When it is not possible to put on tefillin in the morning during the time of davening, they can at least do so throughout the entire day, until sunset. I hope that you will find the appropriate words to influence your Jewish friends.

The calculations of Hashem Yisbarach cannot be known, and it is possible that this is one of the reasons why one is kept in a certain place. When he fulfills this, it is possible that he will then return home, with the consent of the government...

(From a letter dated 22 Kislev, 5712)


## יו"ד שבט

## 228

As discussed at the farbrengen, this is based on the halacha regarding the acquisition of four amos. This is even more significant than standing behind a wall, for a wall acts as a partition—even when it has cracks, it partitions in various respects—whereas this is not the case with four amos; and the rest is understood.

Regarding the mention of the version of Rava with an aleph, I believe I explicitly mentioned at the farbrengen that this is the case in Yalkut Shimoni (Melachim II, 3) and in Maseches Pesachim (117a), and one should examine the Dikdukei Sofrim for other sources.

With a blessing regarding the significance of this day, Rosh Hashanah La’ilanot, for man is the tree of the field, and especially a talmid chacham (Taanis 7a).
(From a letter, 15 Shevat, 5724)

This is a matter that the baal yahrtzeit exerted himself in greatly, and he urged everyone to exert themselves in this. The words of the tzaddikim endure, and the merit of anyone who exerts himself in this is great, especially one who is a rav for his congregation. With respect and a blessing for great success in the aforementioned.
(From a telegram, 14 Shevat, 5726)

... It is understood that the purpose of 10 Shevat is not for trips for the sake of leisure or the like, especially since this also involves bitul Torah. There must be some spiritual reward, not merely simple pleasure (taanug), which is related to the term *helem* (concealment) and *hester* (hiddenness).

Another point—and it is also surprising that it was not mentioned at all—is that this year 10 Shevat falls on Erev Shabbos. There must be sufficient time for ratzo v'shov in due time after the gathering. Perhaps the intention was to do this on the evening of 10 Shevat...
(From a letter, 27 Teves, 5724)

## 233

You note in your letter that the levayah took place in Vancouver on 28 Sivan, which, according to the time in Eretz Yisrael, was the night of the 29th. It seems your intention is that this makes a difference regarding the recitation of Kaddish (the conclusion of the eleven months), for we calculate the yahrtzeit according to the day of passing (not the burial), even in the first year (today is 13 Shevat).

In my opinion, since the recitation of Kaddish is for the merit of the niftar and relates to his judgment, in every instance we follow the time of the place of passing, not that of the place of the mourners.

If there is a practical difference regarding the yahrtzeit (such as when the passing occurred at the time mentioned above), this is debated among the later authorities in Kol Bo (by Rabbi Grunwald) and others. The first opinion holds that we follow the time of the mourners, and he brings support from the sefer Divrei HaSadeh. Others, based on the responsa of the Ksav Sofer (Yoreh Deah, 188), say we follow the place of passing. This is not the place to elaborate. We conclude with good.
(From a letter, Menachem Av, 5716?)

This is regarding the practical action.
Regarding the feeling — the matter has already been stated several times.
And the *zman grama* (time-bound factor) — *Shabbos* (the week of) *Shirah*.
And especially since in every situation — the Torah is light, and "he who trusts in *Hashem*, loving-kindness shall surround him".
(From a letter dated 8 Shevat, 5751)


## ט"ו בשבט

## 237

And this is especially relevant as we stand on the day of Rosh Hashanah for trees, when new powers are added to the plant world. After all, "man is the tree of the field," and furthermore, all categories of *domem* (inanimate), *tzomei'ach* (vegetative), *chai* (animate), and *medaber* (speaking) are found within man, in accordance with the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, that everything in the world has its counterpart in man (who is called a *olam katan* — a microcosm). However, the *medaber* in man, and even the *chai*, are more closely related to the *neshamah* and its matters. This is not the case for the *tzomei'ach* aspect, which pertains to the realm of the body, including its healing and its state of proper health, and so on. Yet, the body and its matters in every single one of *Bnei Yisrael* are also included in spiritual life. In the language of the great teacher, the Rambam—whose profession was that of a physician of both the soul and the body—the body being healthy and whole is one of the ways of Hashem (*Hilchos De'os*, beginning of Chapter 4).

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

(From a letter of Tu B'Shvat, 5727)


## יתרו

## 237

### Yisro

...We are accustomed here to write [the Name of Hashem] with a letter omitted. See Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken, Orach Chaim, end of section 85, and the sources cited there. And this is not the place to elaborate.
[quotation](From a letter dated 8 Cheshvan, 5713)[/quotation]

...Wherever the Name of the Creator is written in Yiddish—and the same applies to English—it should be written with a hyphen (G-d), and not in its complete form, for according to several Acharonim, the sanctity of the Name applies to it...
[quotation](From a letter dated 21 Iyar, 5714)[/quotation]

...General note: I have always wondered why people are not careful to write and print "G-d," and not...

## 239

Page 7: "Three stars." It is common practice not to distinguish between large and small [stars], etc., and therefore one should write "when it becomes night" and the like.

Page 8: Kiddush on milk. Although one can find a basis for this, it is highly questionable. The Birkei Yosef and Shaarei Teshuvah—cited in the Mishnah Berurah, section 272—explicitly rule that one should not make Kiddush or Havdalah on milk.

Page 10: See section 285, which states that the mitzvah is to review the weekly parsha on Erev Shabbos, and only in cases of duress is it done on Shabbos.

On the same page: There are Shabbosos toward the end of the summer when two parshios are read on a single Shabbos.

Page 11: Omit the matter of Havdalah on milk, and also add to the order of Havdalah that one recites "Hinei Keil Yeshuasi."

Page 13: The prohibition of carrying applies also to a Karmelis, not only to a Reshus HaRabim. Furthermore, the explanation of how to construct an Eiruv should be omitted, as the laws of Eiruvin are extremely complex and not as the reader would understand from what is written there. The same applies to Eiruvei Techumin; since it is not the primary focus of this book, it should be omitted, as one must also include the houses outside the city, etc., along with several other details.

Page 14: The statement that Shammai HaZakein is "Beis Shammai" is incomprehensible, as the discussion concerns Hillel and Shammai themselves, not their students.

Page 15: The statement that Shabbos is for all people is contrary to the law that a non-Jew who observes Shabbos is liable for death. Therefore, it should be omitted, as should the story about "we have a spice, and its name is Shabbos," which a simple person will not understand.

Pages 16, 17, and 18: The entire matter of the Sambation should be omitted, as its location is the subject of great dispute, and not as the author writes simply that it is in the south of the land of Ethiopia. Furthermore, many challenge the accounts of the travels of R' Gershon, especially the conclusion regarding "do not kindle a fire," which interprets the verse according to the Karaite interpretation.

Page 20: Delete the word "exact," because our molad is the mean molad, not the true one. The Maftir for Shabbos Rosh Chodesh begins with "U'v'yom HaShabbos," not "U'v'rashei Chodsheichem." Also, omit the word "pious," as this is a custom brought in the Shulchan Aruch...
[quotation](From a letter dated 21 Iyar, 5714)[/quotation]


## משפטים

## 240

### Mishpatim

Although a long time has passed without receiving news from you, I will assume you are in good standing, with peace and health accompanying you in both spiritual and material matters. This is especially so in light of the ruling of the great teacher, the Rambam (Hilchos Deos, beginning of Chapter 4), that the health and wholeness of the body are among the ways of Hashem—and all the more so the health of the soul and its concerns. And in this context, [I refer to] your activities in the institute which you have merited and succeeded in heading. Incidentally, if additional books and publications have appeared, you will surely not withhold the good from sending them here, as has been your good custom in the past; thank you in advance.

Regarding the current matter:
I have learned that the Minister of Justice has appointed a committee of jurists tasked with proposing a series of laws to replace the existing civil law in the area of contract law, buying and selling, leasing, and the like—laws that currently exist in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) as remnants of previous regimes. Among the committee members are also representatives of the religious sector. Furthermore, the committee members have been granted the authority to consult with whomever they find necessary regarding all matters pertaining to this field.

I have also learned from experts in this field that in this area of contract law, negotiations, etc., it is especially possible to make improvements due to the confusion and muddle of several existing laws. Moreover, and most importantly, the opposition from the non-religious side to implementing the laws of the Torah in this part of *Choshen Mishpat* would be minimal. Naturally, however, one must extract and collect from *Choshen Mishpat* the laws pertaining to the aforementioned area and incorporate them into the aforementioned framework with appropriate phrasing, for the phrasing certainly carries weight and will influence the success of the endeavor to base civil laws on the foundation of our Torah, the Torah of life. It is understood and also simple that if the aforementioned endeavor succeeds, there will be well-founded prospects to facilitate the propaganda and action to transfer, step by step, the other areas of jurisdiction in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) to the laws of the Torah.

Since organizing a group of *talmidei chachamim* to deal with the above—for the time being regarding the area of contracts, etc.—is a complicated matter for several reasons, both in terms of the substance of the matter and in terms of organization, expenses, etc., it occurred to me that the most direct path to actual implementation (since time is of the essence, so as not to miss the opportunity) is that the members of the institute, who are already dealing with such things—and surely some of them are specifically in the aforementioned field—can be selected from among them as being capable of this specific work. And since, according to reports, the lawyer [name redacted] is an agreeable person, etc., and would be interested, even from a religious standpoint, in actualizing the above, it is possible that the matter could be resolved with great success.

I shall rely on your interest and your understanding, and I will not elaborate further on what has been said. It would please me to learn of your response to all the above, and primarily of the actions taken to bring the matter to

## 241

actual fruition, and simply, with a strict guarding of the point that this Torah shall not be exchanged.

With respect and blessing, and regards to his father, the Rav, *shlita*.
(From a letter, 25 Sivan, 5722)

...And regarding your writing that this leads to conflicts with [name redacted] and his family—there is a clear ruling in our holy Torah that one who does not wish to have a *din Torah* before the *mara d’asra* (at the very least in a *zeh b’zeh*) is acting and working against the Torah, which is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is one with His wisdom. Consequently, he is harming himself, his household, and all who assist him—a harm not only in the World to Come, but also in this world, in material terms. However, the *Ribono shel Olam*, who is a merciful Father, is patient with him for a time, perhaps in the end he will do *teshuvah* with kindness and mercy and return from his rebellion against Hashem. From this it is also understood that anyone who has a conflict with [name redacted] regarding the above is actually his true friend, and anyone who assists [name redacted] is a companion to [name redacted]’s *yetzer hara*, whose profession it is to incite him to fight against the Torah and its *mitzvos*.
(From a letter, 25 Iyar, 5721)

...Regarding Gehennom, etc. See also Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah (Chapter 8, Halacha 5 and onwards), and there it states, "There is no way in this world to attain it" (the reward; and from this it is understood regarding its opposite—the punishment. See there).
Regarding the *hatra'ah* (warning)—even when the warning is for death in the literal sense, one does not know the essence and quality of the pain of death in reality, except that they tell him the pain is incomparable, etc., and that suffices...
(From a letter, 5730)

B"H, Tuesday, on which it was doubled "it is good",
Parshas "If you lend money" to My people,
5747. Brooklyn, N.Y.
The Administration of the Gemilas Chasadim Society Shomrei Shabbos

Peace and blessing!
I received with pleasure your letter bearing good news that the annual *Melaveh Malkah* of the Gemilas Chasadim Society Shomrei Shabbos will take place on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Mishpatim, Parshas Shekalim, *Mevarchim HaChodesh* Adar, Parshas "If you lend money," etc.—and tomorrow is Rosh Chodesh.
May it be Hashem's will that it be at a good and successful time. The essence of *gemach* is good (for Heaven and for people alike) and brings success.
Especially since this is Motzaei Shabbos Shekalim—the *mitzvah* of *machatzis hashekel*, which also hints at the general concept of *tzedakah*, and we read: "When you take the census of the Children of Israel."
And this is also Motzaei Shabbos *Mevarchim* the month of Adar, whose *mazal* is "healthy" for every one of the Children of Israel, and furthermore, according to the version of the Rosh, that the *mazal* is strong.
And this "health" and strength are increased with greater intensity and greater power through our deeds and our *avodah* in general, and especially through *tzedakah* and *gemach*, and specifically because it is with one's money, one's body, and one's soul—the unity of all the matters of

## 243

a person, in a *mitzvah* that is equal to all the *mitzvos*,
which also makes peace and unites all the Children of Israel. For *gemach* is for both the poor and the rich.
And this year is the year of *Shemitah*, which equates the poor and the rich in all the land, field, and vineyard.
And all of us as one, "May our Father bless us with the light of His countenance"—down to the lowest level, for a person eats the fruits of *gemach* in this world.
And especially since you have surely united and are uniting the Children of Israel by making the private home of every single Jew a house of Torah, prayer, and *gemilas chasadim*, in accordance with the content of the general letter between 10 Shevat and 15 Shevat[ednref_3_*].
May it be Hashem's will that all this will hasten even more the fulfillment of the prayer and the prophecy in the Book of David, for this is the feast of David, King Mashiach—
"You have favored, Hashem, Your land", "our land shall yield its produce," "to dwell in glory in our land," for it will be fulfilled: "Show us, Hashem, Your kindness, and grant us Your salvation", and in a manner of "Show us," "and all flesh shall see"—with physical eyes, literally.
And this is also a Rosh Chodesh feast—for they are renewed like it and glorify their Creator in the name of the honor of His kingdom.
Enclosed is my participation, *bli neder*.
With respect and blessing for success in the above.
