...Regarding your question about traveling to Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) or spending the money to buy a *Sefer Torah*.
In my opinion, you should give the money to a *Gemilas Chasadim* fund, for in that case, the money remains intact for the most part (since a very small percentage are those who do not repay a *gemilas chasadim*), and this serves as an enduring merit for the one who gives the money. There can be two ways in this: to give the money specifically for a *gemach* fund in our Holy Land (may it be built and established) or generally—that is, both for Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) and for outside the land. And if you wish, you can deposit the money into one of the *gemach* funds that are located in my secretariat.
And may the *Ribono shel Olam* give you, and He will give you, long life and good years, so that you may be able from time to time to add to this *gemach* fund, both from your own [funds] and

## 256

from the money that you will take for this purpose from your children and friends, may they live.
(From a letter, 23 Adar, 5714)

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write about closing the contract and about *heter iska*.
The text of the *heter iska* can be found in several books, and among them in the *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch* published by Rabbi Feldman. In your case of a contract, this is easier than a simple loan. If you do not find the text, you can add the words "according to *heter iska*," which will suffice until a Rav can draw up an exact text. If the words "according to *heter iska*" can be written on the contract, that is certainly good. If, for whatever reason, it cannot be written on the contract, one can write on a separate paper: "That the contract between so-and-so, which was made on such-and-such a day, is according to *heter iska*, and on this I come on [date], [year], [city], signed [name]—and then it should be written—before us, the undersigned witnesses, the aforementioned matter was done, and before us signed [name] and [name], with their own hands, signed [name] witness, and signed [name] witness..."
(From a letter, 12 Adar, 5717)

...Regarding his question about obtaining a loan and investing in real estate:
In general, it does not seem right to me—regarding the actual implementation, you should consult with understanding friends...
(From a letter, 21 Menachem Av, 5746)


## אדר

## 257

### Adar

... It is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, that "when Adar enters, we increase in joy." One should examine the end of Maseches Taanis, where the discussion concerns the matter of building for joy. See also the Mishnah there, which concludes with the aspiration that the Beis Hamikdash be rebuilt speedily in our days. This is the joy of Knesses Yisrael below and the joy of Hashem above. And the Kohanim, in private and with heartfelt desire, must prepare through their holy avodah for the building of the Beis Hamikdash in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, amen.
(From a letter, 1 Adar, 5712)

... And in this month of Adar, regarding which our Sages said in the Midrash that its *mazal* is fish—this is a matter for Jews, and especially for Chassidim, of whom it is said, "And they shall multiply like fish within the land." This means that even in worldly and physical matters, they conduct themselves like fish: they do not depart from the source of their life (Berachos 61b), and likewise, they do not depart from the path of Torah and mitzvos. Similarly, this *mazal* will bring him near healing and proper health...
(From a letter, 6 Adar, 5712)

I confirm receipt of your letter, in which you also write about your state of health and the improvement therein.
May it be His will that there be a *refuah sheleimah*, and that this *refuah sheleimah* come soon. This includes the matter of sadness that you write about, for a healthy Jew is a joyful Jew.
Especially since we find ourselves in the month of Adar, and we have been instructed from Rosh Chodesh Adar to "increase in joy." A directive from the Torah certainly implies that the Giver of the Torah first provides the ability to fulfill His directive, and also provides reasons so that one can see that the directive has a strong foundation. Surely, it is unnecessary for me to elaborate on this for you...
(From a letter, 7 Adar, 5766)

## 258

I received with pleasure the regards from them, as well as their general and personal letters, through... who also told me about his meeting and conversation with them. I was happy to hear of their progress in their learning and conduct. Surely they will not be satisfied with past achievements but will go from strength to strength, as per the command of our Sages, "we ascend in matters of holiness," for all matters of goodness and holiness are *ein-sof* (infinite), and there is always room for improvement, preference, and beautification.
Since, through *hashgacha pratis*, the response was delayed until Rosh Chodesh—the time we are commanded to increase in joy from its inception (and Adar I is also included)—and the command applies also to the women and daughters of Yisrael, as our Sages informed us, "they too were part of that miracle," and a command of the Torah means the granting of strength and the ability to fulfill it—may it be His will that this be so for each and every one of them, in all matters of goodness, both physically and spiritually.
As requested, I will mention each and every one of them at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of their heart's desires for the good.
With a blessing for success and good tidings.
(From a letter, 1 Rosh Chodesh Adar I, 5767)


## תרומה

## 258

### Terumah

... An opening. At its beginning. The Beis Hamikdash is the foundation of the world, for it is one of the seven things that preceded the world. And the intention is that from there the Shechinah will spread (which is called so because of "And I will dwell among them" — which is stated regarding the making of the Mishkan, which is called a Mikdash) throughout the entire world. And this can be established from the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the *shetiyah* is the Beis Hamikdash (Sanhedrin 26b). And even according to the one who disagrees there regarding the interpretation of the verse, he does not disagree with the essence of the matter, that the Beis Hamikdash is the *shetiyah* and foundation of the world, which are the words of the Sages (Yoma 54b; and like the Rambam in his commentary on the Mishnah there). The Beraisa regarding the seven things that were created before the world was created, etc., including the Beis Hamikdash — is proof of the precedence, but not that it is the foundation of the world and a foundation even in the literal sense. And Torah and Teshuvah, etc., will prove this...
(From a letter, 1 Sivan, 5724)

## 259

I was pleased to learn of the setting of times for the study of our holy Torah in public in the aforementioned shul. And the great importance of holding Torah study classes in a shul certainly requires no elaboration, as it is explained in many places in our holy books and explained well in the holy letters and sichos of our Rebbes, the leaders of our generation, may their merit protect us. I have come only to encourage and prioritize, based on the saying of our Sages, "One only encourages those who are already diligent," to encourage efforts to increase the number of participants in Torah study classes, in the revealed Torah and in the inner dimensions of the Torah which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, and likewise to strive to include all the congregants of the shul in this. And one can hint at this at the beginning and head of this week’s parsha...
(From a letter, 7 Adar, 5724)

I was pleased to receive the notification that the members of the Shas and Mishnayos society of the shul are holding a gathering to mark your tenure of many years as *mara d'asra*. May it be the will of Hashem that in the full sense of this title, you will continue to be the *mara d'asra* of this place, by making the place an *achsanya shel Torah* (an inn for Torah), permeated with fear of Hashem and love of Hashem, which are the root of the 365 negative mitzvos and 248 positive mitzvos, and from them is drawn and comes the fulfillment of the mitzvos in truth. And may you continue to spread the study of our Torah, the Torah of life, both the revealed Torah and the inner dimensions of the Torah, as is the instruction of these days of Chanukah, that one adds in the candle (mitzvah) and (Torah) light from day to day.
With respect and regards to all the participants, and with a blessing for length of days and good and illuminating years.
(From a letter, days of Chanukah, 5727)

*Achsanya shel Torah*: See Bava Metzia 85a, Arachin 16b. (And its reward — Berachos 58a, Pesachim 86b, Yoma 12a, and from the attribute of Chassidus that he does not judge him (Maharik 161 — mentioned in Shach, Choshen Mishpat 67, sub-paragraph 12)).
*Which are the root of the 365 negative mitzvos and 248 positive mitzvos*: Tanya, Chapter 4. Commentary of the Rambam on Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, beginning of Chapter 2.
*In the candle... light*: See Rashi, s.v. *banim* (Shabbos 23b).

## 260

As in my letters from the past — regarding all matters of the shul, both spiritual and material: the *nusach*, customs, management, construction, etc., the committee is the representative of *anash* and my representative, and it is they who judge, determine, and decide both internally and externally, and the question regarding this is a great wonder. May Hashem grant them success in the holy work to establish, expand, and enlarge the shul in quantity and quality, and certainly all *anash* will assist them, and the house will be great in prayer and in the revealed and inner Torah together — as per the instructions of the Baal Shem Tov and the Tzemach Tzedek, until the coming of the Tzemach, who is our righteous Moshiach.
With a blessing for success and for an active gathering in the shul on Shabbos Bereishis, may it come upon us for good.
(From a telegram, 26 Tishrei, 5729)

... Regarding what you wrote about the location for placing the Aron, it should be clarified if there is an issue of changing a custom in this. If it has not been done in a manner of such protrusions from the outside until now, then one should not innovate this matter. As is known, how much they were extremely careful not to make any innovation in the matters of the shul, even in minor things, and even if on the face of it there is no concern in that specific place, for the onlooker will say, "What is different about this change from another change?" And the wise will understand.
(From a letter, 8 Menachem Av, 5715)

... My father-in-law showed me... your letter regarding a *paroches* inside the Aron Kodesh. And what you noted regarding this and the dispute between Tosafos and Rashi in Megillah 26b. However, the dispute between Rashi and Tosafos is only regarding the law of the *paroches* if it should be inside the Aron Kodesh, but this is not a dispute in reality. Therefore, from there, on the contrary, it is proof that there was such a practice to hang a *paroches* inside the Aron Kodesh. And nevertheless, there is a concern in the matter to hang the *paroches* now in our times inside the Aron Kodesh, even if there will be a *paroches* also on the Aron, because this is a change in the custom of the shuls of the children of Israel in the recent generations, at the very least. And it is known how much they were particular about

## 261

changing customs, even in things that did not have any concern of prohibition or the like, and especially in the customs of the shul in this country, which need strengthening even more...
(From a letter, 22 Mar Cheshvan, 5715)

... Regarding what you wrote about the matter of the *paroches*, it is a wonder that you did not interpret my intention as it is. For the matter is not to bring proof that there was a *paroches* outside the Aron Kodesh, for there is no dispute about that, and it was only needed for a source that there is a place for a *paroches* inside the Aron Kodesh. And consequently, all the places where you bring proof that it is evident that there was a *paroches* outside is like the common saying, "He is knocking on an open door." And what I wrote is that from Rashi and even from Tosafos in Megillah, it is proven that there was a *paroches* also inside...
What I wrote "in recent generations" — means that then there was a *paroches* only outside.
(From a letter, 17 Kislev, 5715)

... Regarding what you wrote about there being no *mechitza* between the men and women — my hope is strong that with appropriate effort and in pleasant ways and with words that come from the heart, you will succeed in fixing this. And this matter is extremely important, as it will be a good and beautiful precedent for many communities. And especially since even those who for the time being do not accept the explanation that without a *mechitza* it is against the Shulchan Aruch, one must explain to them in a way that is also appropriate to the simple intellect of the *nefesh habehamis*, that certainly their intention in prayer is also to turn to the One who is higher than them, however they may describe Him in their intellect or in the feeling of the heart. And even according to their view, prayer is a matter of service of the heart and with *kavanah*. And an immediate result of contemplation, even for a short while, on this is that one must remove all matters that interfere with *kavanah* and with connecting to the One to whom they are turning and praying. And one sees tangibly that the absence of a *mechitza*, even if they pray in separate sections of the room, incites the men or women to look at the other section, etc. And it is simple that in the above there is no belittling of anyone's value. And therefore it is also the law (even though the relationship between a father and his children is a matter according to the Torah, and in the style of the verse "As a father has compassion on his children," nevertheless the law in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim 298 is) that it is forbidden to kiss his children in the shul, and the reason for the law is according to what was stated...
(From a letter, 25 Iyar, 5719)

## 262

Regarding what you noted in your letter about a *mechitza* in the shul, a long time ago an article was printed on this in the monthly *HaMaor* which appears in Brooklyn, Teves 5711, by Rabbi Avraham Weinfield of New York. He notes there from the Rambam, Chapter 8 of Hilchos Lulav, from Hilchos Beis HaBechirah Chapter 5, the commentary on the Mishnah in Sukkah, and the Tosafos Yom Tov, that in the latter places it is implied that the *mechitza* must be in a way that they cannot look. He also points to the Responsa of the Maharam Schick, Orach Chaim section 77, who shook the world against those who want to make a *mechitza* with pillars in a way that they can see. And he concluded that it is simple that all this is said even if all the women are careful with head covering and not having an exposed handbreadth, and all the more so if they go with uncovered hair and exposed arms, there is a double prohibition, and see Orach Chaim section 75, and this is simple. And in the aforementioned monthly of the month of Iyar-Sivan 5713, it is also discussed regarding the above.
(From a letter, 9 Tammuz, 5713)

I was pleased to receive in its time your regards through... who also told me about your good deeds and your influence in your surroundings for the benefit of raising the banner of the Israel of old and strengthening the spirit of Judaism. And if in all places and at all times a good deed of a Jew is very, very precious, then all the more so in our time, when the concealments and hiddenness have increased, which are obstacles and delays in every holy and pure thing. And according to what is brought in the letter of the Ramban, "Everything that is holier than its fellow is more desolate than its fellow," then all the more so one must cherish every good deed, and one must utilize every possibility of action or speech for the strengthening of Torah and Judaism. And all the more so and *kal v'chomer* from the members of the tribe and the portion of the tribe whom Hashem chose to be priests before Him and to serve in the holy, whose words and deeds in all the above are many times greater.
It is known that all the details of a person's affairs are by Divine Providence from Him, may He be blessed. And since the matter of the *mechitza* in the shul reached your honor, it is certainly by special Divine Providence, that it is in your honor's hand to act in this. And the elaboration on the great value of the *mechitza* in the shul is certainly superfluous. And if in the Beis Hamikdash in Eretz Yisrael, where they saw miracles tangibly, and as the Mishnah says, "Ten miracles were performed for our forefathers in the Beis Hamikdash," even with all this they were forced to make a *mechitza* between men and women, as is told in Tractate Sukkah and in Hilchos Beis HaBechirah of the Rambam, then all the more so after the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash — may it be rebuilt speedily in our days —, and in the Diaspora, and in a shul which is only a *mikdash me'at* (a small sanctuary), and especially in this orphaned generation, where the matter of the *mechitza* in the shul is necessary more and more. And we have seen tangibly that in those shuls that abolished the *mechitza* or made it too small, it was nothing but the beginning of a departure and a descent from one level to another, G-d forbid. And afterwards they also set up a microphone on Shabbos and Yom Tov, which is a prohibition *d'oraysa*, and their hand is still outstretched to descend many levels backwards. And I do not wish to elaborate on the disgrace of the children of Israel, etc. And my hope, based on the saying of our Sages, "One only encourages those who are already diligent," is that your honor will seize all the means and ways to abolish this evil thought of abolishing the *mechitza* in the shul. And to explain to them — even though it is a simple matter — that when one comes even to a small minister of flesh and blood and asks

## 263

him even for just a small request, it is from the ways of etiquette and also understood by intellect, that at the time of the action one should not do things that are the opposite of the minister's will, for this is in contradiction and opposition to the request and the petition. And all the more so when one comes before the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, and asks for the life of children and sustenance, that it is forbidden and a criminal sin to do at the time of the action things by which one rebels against the word of Hashem, the G-d of the world. And the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, is known: "A *chazakah* (presumption) for *taamulah* (propaganda/outreach) is that it does not return empty." And may Hashem grant your honor success, that easily and in pleasant ways, you will fulfill the mission of the Place, blessed be He, that the shul will remain a house of prayer to Hashem, in which the prayers of Israel will be accepted.
(From a letter, 1 Menachem Av, 5713)

According to the above — it is correct to speak with the homeowners and the president, etc., from which it is clearly seen what the matter of the *mechitza* is, that those who oppose the *mechitza* as it should be — they have revealed their opinion now as to what their true outlook is. And from this it is understood that all those who believe in Torah from Heaven (the opposite of the Conservatives) must fight for the *mechitza*, etc.
This is not an obstacle at all to conducting the aforementioned petition — now or later. And on the contrary, then he will not be able to come out against them strongly as he would like, since by accepting the position he admits that they also have the opinion in spiritual matters, and even if they promise this in a contract — they are changing the contract as they like.
This is not his business at all, and in general it is a matter of great doubt if it is permitted according to law.
(From a letter, 24 Menachem Av, 5724)

... You ask my opinion if it is permitted to pray in a shul that uses a microphone on Shabbos and Yom Tov.
And it is a great wonder that there is doubt in such an alarming matter as mentioned, for the use of a microphone on Shabbos and Yom Tov is a desecration of the days of Shabbos and Yom Tov in public. And in addition to this, it is also "to conquer the queen with me in the house," i.e., in a house of prayer to the Giver of the Torah and its mitzvos, for the mitzvah of Shabbos is equal to all the mitzvos, as our Sages said in Yerushalmi Nedarim (end of Chapter 3).
And since the desecration of Shabbos is done in the name of all the members of this shul, for the *gabbaim* who decide the above are their representatives, there is room for doubt regarding all matters of prayer and reading of the Torah in it, and not only in the part that is transmitted by the microphone, but also those before them and after them.
And now, all the above is from the letter of the law of the laws of Shabbos, if there were no matter of *chillul Hashem* (desecration of G-d's name) in this at all. But when paying attention also to this point, the matter is many times more severe. And in my opinion, it is absolutely simple that even on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur one should pray in private, but G-d forbid in the aforementioned shul...
(From a letter, 25 Elul, 5718)

## 264

After a break, your letter from 23 Shevat was received, in which you write about the matter of the shul.
Now, although in general it is not my way to get involved in such things until they ask my opinion insistently, etc., but since according to my estimation the background is not smooth, and furthermore, and this is also the main thing, that the first principle must be to increase shuls that are on the purity of holiness, especially in our time and in the camp of the good, etc., therefore I expressed my opinion in accordance with this: that although temporarily it is correct for several reasons that your honor should be in the shul about which you write, but regarding permanence — according to the above, it is good that you should establish a shul for yourself. And even if its beginning is small, its end will be very great, and may it be the will that it will be very great.
It is understood that a judge has only what his eyes see, and this is not the type of matter in general to insist specifically on my opinion as stated. But on the other hand, I am not permitted to hide what seems to me to be for the benefit of all those interested and involved — that it should be in the aforementioned way. And even if it is impossible for it to be a shul in his house literally, one must strive for a shul that can be more independent than in the current shul.
And since we are approaching the month of Adar, whose point and the middle of the month are the days of Purim, of "sending portions to one another," and one of the reasons for this is the drawing together of the hearts of all Israel until true unity, may it be the will that this action should begin immediately from the Shabbos when we bless the month of Adar, going and increasing until the moon is in its fullness in the middle of the month.
With respect and a blessing for good tidings in all the above and for true *nachas* from your son, may he live, about whom you write — in the midst of all your children, may they live — together with your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live.
(From a letter, 26 Shevat, 5724)


## תצוה

## 265

### Tetzaveh

...Regarding what is written in the Torah Or, in the maamar beginning with the words "On the 25th of Kislev," concerning the matter of the lighting of the candles in the Beis Hamikdash — in this discourse, it explains the opinion of the poskim that the lighting of the candles was only in the evening, and they were positioned east and west (Responsa of the Rashba; Ramban; Tosafos, s.v. "U'leheitiv," Yoma 71a; and see Tosefos Yom Tov, Chapter 7 of Yoma and Chapter 3 of Tamid). It explains the order in the morning: the cleaning of the seventh candle, the cleaning of the sixth candle, the lighting of the sixth candle, and the lighting of the seventh candle. The discussion is lengthy, and this is not the place to elaborate.
(From a letter, days of Chanukah, 5720)

...The Torah thought she shared was well-received. Thank you. And surely she knows what is explained in the sefarim, that within every one of the Bnei Yisrael, the altar is their heart, and it contains an external and an internal heart, analogous to the external and internal altars.
(From a letter, 12 Adar II, 5786)


## פורים קטן

## 265

### Purim Katan

...And especially since this day itself causes it to be Purim Katan, which—along with its month, Adar I—is also included in the directive of Chazal, "When Adar enters, we increase in joy." May it be the will [of Hashem] that this joy be drawn down from this month and these days to the entire year, and that it be a joy appropriate to the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, the Torah of Chassidus: a joy of the soul and also a joy of the body, a joy from physical matters and a joy from spiritual matters, which will come through health and true expansion of the mind.

And in the clever phrasing of the expression, "this small one shall be great"—from this Purim Katan, of which it is said that even a "small" joy breaks through barriers, may all Bnei Yisrael, and each one of us among them, merit the fulfillment of the promise, "You shall take the head of the Bnei Yisrael," to bring them out from the straits and limitations into the expanse in all their matters.

[quotation](From a letter dated 14 Adar, 5717)[/quotation]


## פורים

## 266

### Purim

As we approach the upcoming days of Purim, when each of us will hear the Megillah and contemplate the narrative it tells, we wish to draw attention to several details regarding what transpired *bayamim hahem bizman hazeh* (in those days, at this time).

A Haman HaAgagi arose and issued a decree *lehashmid uleharog et kol hayehudim* (to destroy and to kill all the Jews) on a set date.

Esther HaMalkah says: "Go, assemble all the Jews and fast"—and then she would attempt to annul the decree.

Mordechai goes and gathers tens of thousands of Jewish children and teaches them Torah. He teaches them how they will offer the *minchat ha'omer* when the Beis Hamikdash is fully rebuilt.

These children become so captivated that even seeing the mortal danger before their eyes, they all cry out: "We remain with Mordechai, with the Torah—whether for life or for death!"

And on that very day, the decree is nullified. Haman’s downfall is already sealed. The Jews are completely saved, even though they only learn of it several months later.

*Maaseh avot siman labanim* (the deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children).

*Et tzarah hi leYaakov* (it is a time of trouble for Yaakov). A new Haman has issued a decree *lehashmid, etc.*—may it not be and may it not happen.

We must know that one of the primary means to nullify the decree—one of the primary means to ensure *vehashivot leHaman et gemulo berosho velyehudim tahyeh orah vesimcha* (and to return Haman’s recompense upon his own head, and for the Jews there was light and joy)—is to gather Jewish children and teach them Torah and Yiddishkeit;

To tell them that the *Geulah Sheleimah* lies in our own hands, and consequently there is no place for despair, for as soon as Jews do *teshuvah*, they are immediately redeemed;

To tell them that *bimheirah yibaneh Beis Hamikdash* and that we must all be worthy and prepared to serve the *Ribono shel Olam*!

And on that very day that Jewish children become imbued with this spirit; on that very day that they are ready to cry out: "We are with you—with your Torah we stand—whether for life or for death"—on that very day, the Torah assures us, the decree is nullified. Haman

## 267

meets his wretched end, and for all Jews there will be, in the very near future, *orah vesimcha vesasson viykar* (light, joy, gladness, and honor).

With wishes for a happy Purim.
(From a letter, Adar II, 5705)

---

...In addition to confirming your letter and the booklet, and in addition to my telegram—although my remark regarding *matanos la'evyonim* is self-understood and requires no explanation—I wish to use this opportunity to add another point on this matter. It is this:

Beyond the primary aspect, which is the religious value of the mitzvah of *matanos la'evyonim*—which is one of the mitzvos of the day of Purim, and indeed, as explained in the words of the Rambam, even more elevated than the matter of *mishloach manos*—there is in this a pedagogical value: to educate and accustom children to overcome the trait of childhood (?) and to give their money to those to whom they owe nothing at all. This carries a deeper emotion than sending *mishloach manos* to a friend. Especially since the separation of *tzedakah* from one’s own money should lead—or at the very least, through the influence of the educator who encourages this—to *tzedakah* through one’s own body and labor. These are the most active guides to weakening the feeling of selfishness, which is the source of all kinds of outbursts and disturbances, leading even to actual *chet* and *avon*.

I will not deny that as a *chossid*, this point is especially dear to me, for it is among the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus and its proponents to emphasize how the love of Hashem and the love of the Torah and its *mitzvos* are one with the love of Israel, to the point that they are all one.
(From a letter, 13 Nissan, 5723)

---

...Surely you utilized the days of Purim, and as it is written in the Megillah that "many of the people of the land became Jews" (*mityahadim*). One of the allusions in this is that those who, before Purim, were "people of the land" (*amei ha'aretz*)—meaning they occupied themselves only with worldly matters—became *Yehudim* (Jews). According to the *drash* and the language of our Sages, Israel are called *Yehudim* because they deny *avodah zarah* (idolatry). The *pnimiyus* (inner meaning) of this is that in every thing, one seeks—and consequently finds—divinity. For one who says that there is an *atar panui minei* (a place void of Him)—this is a matter of *shtei rashuyot* (two authorities), a form of *avodah zarah*. *Vedu'k*.
(From a letter, 19 Adar, 5716)


## תשא

## 268

### Tisa

...Regarding the point raised by your honor in the compilation on Parshas Ki Tisa—that since one cannot prohibit something that is not his, Aharon did not transgress the prohibition of avodah zarah with the gold of the Eigel, as he did not acquire it—this is not the case. For even before it was fashioned into an idol, and even at the very beginning of its making, one transgresses the negative commandment of "You shall not make for yourself a graven image," as explained in the Rambam, etc.

The incident of the Eigel took place before the Oral Torah was taught to the Bnei Yisrael; they were obligated only in what was explicitly stated in the Aseres Hadibros: 1) the act of making, 2) an idol. And even if you were to say that they had learned beforehand and fulfilled the four hundred chapters of avodah zarah that Avraham Avinu taught Yaakov (Zohar Vol. III, 105a; 202b)—the fulfillment of this stringency on their own initiative does not override the saving of a life (*pikuach nefesh*) for Aharon [after he saw the killing of Chur (cited in Rashi)].

This is unlike the principle that one cannot prohibit something that is not his. Many of the discussions in the compilation—which are logical arguments (and note the Tosafos in Shevuos 22b, end of side b)—must hold true even before the study of the Oral Torah. Therefore, they were included in the compilation.

In the same vein, the well-known question regarding the matters of *Chafetz Chaim* is resolved simply: How did Yisrael perform the bris milah at night (Shemos Rabbah 19:5)?

The answer is that the law that milah must be performed during the day was introduced only after the Giving of the Torah (Tosafos, s.v. *Mar*, Yevamos 72b). And even if you were to say that they observed this as well before the Torah was given, they did not forgo the eating of the Korban Pesach—which is forbidden to the uncircumcised—on account of this stringency.

Enclosed is the discussion of the student regarding the above, which I hope will interest your honor.
(From a letter dated 11 Nissan, 5733)

...On this occasion, I would like to draw your honor’s attention to what I have seen in several Pagi publications: the depiction of the Luchos with a semi-circular top. This is a custom of the nations of the world, the opposite—lehavdil—of the words of our Sages, who stated that they were six [handbreadths] long, six wide, and three thick (Bava Basra 14a). In our publications, and especially for children, we are precise about this (as enclosed).
(From a letter dated 12 Shevat, 5727)


## א. רשות ונתינת­כח לרופא לרפאות

## 271

### A. The Permission and Empowerment of the Physician to Heal

On this occasion, I would like to express my appreciation to you, as it is evident from the words of the Rabbanit—may she live—that you have encouraged her spirit. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, you will not only heal the bodies of the patients who come to you, but also encourage their spirits and strengthen their trust in Hashem.

It is well known that regarding the statement of our Sages that King Chizkiyahu hid the Book of Remedies, the Rambam already cautioned that this statement should not be interpreted as being against the science of medicine. He explains that it was a book of charms (Commentary on the Mishnah by the Rambam, Pesachim, end of Chapter 4; Moreh Nevuchim, Part 3, Chapter 37), and that the Torah has granted permission (and according to Chassidus, this also means power) to the physician to heal.

Although the opinion of the Ibn Ezra (Shemos 21:19) is that this applies only to illnesses caused by external factors and not internal ones (see also the Ramban in his introduction to his commentary on the Torah and at the beginning of Parshas Bechukosai, cited in the Taz to Yoreh Deah, end of Section 336), it is already a widespread custom in Israel, following the Rambam, to utilize medical treatments while trusting in Hashem that He will send His word—through a specific person and a specific remedy—and heal them.
(From a letter, 1 Elul, 5711)

It is known that medicine corrects a situation from this point forward (Kesuvos 74b), but it is also possible to uproot the entire [matter] from its source (see Chullin 48a; Responsa Tzafnas Paneach, Part 1, Section 14). Now, the vitality and health of the body depend on the soul, and the vitality and health of the soul of a Jewish person depend on Torah and Mitzvos. As our Sages have said, the 248 positive commandments correspond to the 248 limbs, and the 365 negative commandments correspond to the 365 sinews (Zohar, Part 1, 170b). This is not merely a symbolic numerical correspondence; rather, it is because of the actual connection between these matters that they are equal in number (see Tanya, Chapter 51).

In the healing of a person in the spiritual sense—the healing of the soul, from which the healing of the body evolves—there are also these two modes: whether one merely corrects the situation from this point forward, or uproots the matter from its source. This is achieved through avodah from yirah or from ahavah (Yoma 86a). Through avodah from ahavah, no trace remains of the previous inappropriate state in the spiritual realm, and one returns to their full strength in both the physical and spiritual sense—to the "strength" in the body through the revelation of the "strength" in the soul (see Kuntres Acharon in Tanya, discourse beginning *V'tzedakah K'nachal*; Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Re'eh, discourse beginning *Anochi Notein Lifneichem Hayom Bracha*).
(From a letter, 26 Menachem Av, 5713)

In response to your letter—which lacks a date—regarding the question of the local physician (see also Sanhedrin, end of Chapter 1, and especially according to the commentary of the Rambam, Hilchos De'os, end of Chapter 4), it is understood that in such matters, everyone must consult together, as in any matter concerning the public and the collective of Kfar Chabad. In any case, may it be the will of Hashem that the residents of the village experience the healing of the "Healer of all flesh and Performer of wonders," as He says in His Torah, the Torah of life: "I am Hashem your Healer"—and therefore—"I will not place upon you any of the diseases..." which is the most sublime form of healing.
(From a letter, 28 Tishrei, 5717)

I am pleased to receive news from the esteemed Chassid... regarding your attitude toward him, your care for his affairs, and above all, your attention to everything the Rabbi... needs.

It is already known from the statement of our Sages (Bava Basra 9b) that one who gives a coin, etc., is blessed with six, whereas one who consoles him is blessed with eleven. If our Sages generally derived from "He shall surely heal" (*verapo yerapei*) that the Torah granted permission to the physician to heal, yet there was a concern that perhaps people would rely on the physician himself and forget "G-d who made him"—which is the reason why Chizkiyahu hid the Book of Remedies according to many commentators—then when the physician himself knows that he is merely the emissary of the "Healer of all flesh and Performer of wonders," who is Hashem our G-d, then naturally there is no room for this concern, and his medical treatments are most successful. May Hashem send blessing and success in your work, that you may be the proper emissary to bring healing to the pains of the people whom Divine Providence brings to your hand. And "the reward of a mitzvah is a mitzvah," that in your own personal affairs as well, blessing and success shall be drawn down for what you, your wife, and your children need, in both physical and spiritual matters.
(From a letter, 11 Nissan, 5713)

After your silence, I was pleased to receive your letter of the 5th of Iyar, and I thank you for the good news regarding your health. Surely you are fulfilling the command of our holy Torah, which informs us that it is the Torah that grants permission to the physician to heal. In this context, "permission" also means "power," and the physician is nothing more than a channel through which one receives strength and additional strength for the body to be healthy and whole, which is one of the ways of Hashem, as explained in the Rambam, Hilchos De'os, beginning of Chapter 4, and in many other places, as well as in the teachings of Chassidus in several discourses.

Since we are in the days between Pesach, the time of our freedom, and the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah—"engraved (*charut*) on the tablets," read not *charut* but *cheirut* (freedom)—may it be the will of Hashem that each of you experiences an increase in freedom from all matters that distract from the service of Hashem. This includes matters of physical health, as explained in the teachings of our Sages, that all of Israel were healthy and whole for the receiving of the Torah, even in their bodies and in the physical sense.

This is understood even more deeply according to what is explained in Tanya, Chapter 49, regarding "And He chose us from all nations and tongues," that the choice is revealed specifically in the material body, etc., see there.
With blessings for good news in health.
(From a letter, 14 Iyar, 5717)

I have received the news regarding your health, and my hope is that from day to day you see improvement in this.

Certainly, for someone like you, it is superfluous to emphasize the command of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, which grants permission to the physician to heal. From this, it is understood that one must follow the instructions of the physician. Although sometimes the thought arises that one is "wasting time" on medical matters, rest, and the like, even with a slight contemplation it is understood from the aforementioned statement of our Sages that this is not a waste; rather, on the contrary, because through the short time that (to physical eyes) one "wastes," one gains much more time afterward, which one can utilize with joy and a good heart to serve Hashem "in all your ways," as per the instruction of our Sages, explained in detail in the teachings of Chassidus, regarding the verse "In all your ways know Him."
With blessings for a speedy recovery and good news in all the aforementioned.
(From a letter, 24 Nissan, 5717)

...And during the days of the month of Kislev, the month of redemption, you must work upon yourself to conduct yourself according to the instruction of our Sages, who commanded to listen to the voice of the physicians and to do so with joy. What difference does it make in what manner and in what matters you fulfill the will of the Creator, as long as you do it without calculations? When Hashem says to listen to the physician, one must do so and be satisfied with the opportunity to listen to the will of Hashem; naturally, this must be done with joy, and then Hashem helps, and one sees that there is indeed something to be satisfied with.

I hope that you will write to me that you are doing this, and may Hashem add His blessing to you and to your entire household, that you may live in proper health and with ample livelihood.
Awaiting good news.
(From a letter, 3 Kislev, 5714)

After a long interruption, I was pleased to receive your letter of the 12th of Adar II.

Regarding what you write concerning the words of the doctors: It is a known principle and the conduct of every Jew that one must conduct oneself according to the instructions of our holy Torah. Since our Sages tell us that "the Torah granted permission to the physician to heal," this is a clear indication that the physician is an emissary. Even if the emissary does not always know the inner intent, what the emissary says regarding the practical action comes from the Sender (Hashem). In such a manner, this is a matter of Torah. Therefore, it is understandable that even if one does not fully understand, or if there are questions about the emissary—as you write in your letter—this should not have any influence on the obedience to do what the doctor says. Therefore, I am certain that upon receiving this letter, you will begin to follow what the doctor says. May Hashem grant that the following and doing according to their instruction should be with great success in all matters.

Also, it goes without saying that the conduct of not eating on time, eating only once a day, and the like, is entirely not the way of the Baal Shem Tov, about which we have heard many times from our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, that there must be "you shall surely help him" (*azov ta'azov imo*)—with the body—but not through fasts and self-afflictions.

I hope to receive a quick answer from you that you are beginning to do as stated above. May it be His will that it should be with success.
(From a letter, 19 Adar II, 5717)

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you also write about your conduct, especially regarding eating. In matters connected with the health of the body, our holy Torah, the Torah of the living G-d, instructs that one must follow everything the doctor says, for "the Torah granted permission to the physician," and he is no more than an emissary. Naturally, one can tell the doctor the arguments and reasoning that exist, and also the reasoning you write to me, but after the doctor hears the arguments, one must follow his instructions, without distinction as to whether they agree with your reasoning or not. As stated above, the doctor is no more than an emissary who acts with the power and permission that the Torah gave him.

Since this originates from the Torah, it is a benefit for the body and the soul alike. Even if one does not understand this, or it seems otherwise, this is also no wonder, for the Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He, and it is no wonder that a person does not understand everything that is in the Torah. However, a person must fulfill everything that is in the Torah even without understanding, and "the end of understanding is to come."

I hope that you will follow everything said above, and do so with joy and a good heart.
With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.
(From a letter, 22 Iyar, 5717)

In response to your letter—undated—in which you write that the doctor told your wife—may she live—that she needs to be in the hospital for a few days for investigation and examination, and your wife is fearful and anxious about the hospital due to various concerns (which have no basis):

You must explain to her in words appropriate to her current state of mind that:
The Almighty created the world and He leads the world, both in the lower hemisphere where we are, and in the upper hemisphere where... and you are. "He spoke and it came to be," "He commanded and it stood firm." Everything that happens in the world does not happen without the Almighty, and everything the Almighty wants happens. It is just that the Almighty wants us to make a vessel in nature, which means that matters should be carried out in the way of nature.

When a Jew, man or woman, does not feel well and one needs to call a doctor, it does not mean that the doctor will do as he pleases; rather, the content of this is that Hashem has chosen the doctor to be His emissary to carry out the mission through him.

And when one has trust in the Almighty, without doubts, that He leads the world, then one is privileged to see this also with physical eyes, at every step: how the Almighty holds each one of us by the hand and leads us as is best for us, both physically and spiritually.

Consequently, if she goes to the hospital according to the doctor's instructions, she still remains under the Almighty's domain. And the Almighty will watch over her and see that it goes as is best for her, both for the health of the body and for the health of the soul.

She only needs to be strong in her faith and trust that what the Rebbe—my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—blessed her with will certainly be fulfilled; he blessed her then, blesses her now, and will continue to bless her that she should have a recovery. May you and she soon be able to report good news, that she feels healthy.

Presumably, she puts money into the charity box of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes before Shabbos and Yom Tov for lighting candles, and you surely say the Rebbe's chapter of Tehillim, which is currently Chapter 71, at least until the 10th of Shevat, 5711. Of course, all this is without a vow.
With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*, awaiting good news.
(From a letter, 16 Elul, 5710)

Your letter of the 24th of Tammuz has been received. Regarding your question about your health—cease thinking about this entirely. Instead, turn to a doctor and fulfill in practice his instructions regarding your daily schedule, etc., without occupying your power of thought with this. Likewise, regarding what you wrote about your sister—may she live—she also should have consulted with a doctor. Our Sages have said that the Torah grants permission to the physician to heal. For everything, our Sages said there must be a hold in nature. May the "Healer of all flesh" send their healing.
(From a letter, 29 Tammuz, 5716)


## ב. רופא מומחה

## 276

### B. A Specialist Physician

In response to your letters from the 27th of Sivan and thereafter, in which you write regarding your state of health and the opinions of several physicians you have consulted, and consequently what has occurred to you, etc.

In such a matter, it is appropriate that during the Month of Mercy — Elul — there be a consultation (*consilium*) of two specialist physicians whom you have visited and who have examined you. You should explain your reasoning and rationale to them, and thereafter act according to their instruction; for the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal.

(From a letter dated 18 Tammuz, 5717)

## 277

The response to your letter — which was received with a much longer delay than usual — is that at an *eis ratzon* (time of favor), your *pidyon nefesh* regarding your son, may he live, will be read at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever he requires, and especially for the improvement of his health in the near future.

It is puzzling that you write that you are consulting with a physician, yet add that he is not a specialist in your specific ailment but rather an internist. Even though it has already been said that "there is salvation in a multitude of counselors," it is understood and simple that the primary consultant must be a specialist in the field, and there are several specialists in this field in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established. If this is the case regarding routine treatment, it is all the more so regarding treatment with a new medication, as such medications generally require extra caution, as experience has shown.

It is understood that if a specialist physician prescribes treatment with medicinal substances that are found only in the United States, then efforts should be made to send them from here, provided that the physician writes the name of the substances in detail (in the language of medical texts, in Latin characters) along with the necessary information for this. For example, as you mention in your letter regarding pills: many of these substances come in pills of different sizes and the like. When you tell a specialist physician that you are writing about this to someone overseas, he will certainly know how to specify the substances.

In general, the suggestion is correct that for some time, at least, the aforementioned should reduce his studies and engage in physical labor, or at least in office work. If he refuses this, as you write in your letter, it should be clarified that this is a matter of "there is a time to act for Hashem, [even if it means] nullifying Your Torah," as the great teacher, the Rambam, also writes in *Hilchos Deios*, end of Chapter 3 and beginning of Chapter 4.

Since, according to the content of your letter, you are engaged in the "healing of the soul" for your sons, these students, it is understood according to the measure of the Holy One, blessed be He — *midah k'neged midah* (measure for measure) — that your reward will be doubled regarding the healing of your sons in the literal sense. Furthermore, according to the language of the Rambam, the soul has health and illness just as the body does (*Shemonah Perakim* by the Rambam, Chapter 3, and *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 2). We see in the healing of the body that it is possible [to heal] through bitter or sweet substances, and the distinction is understood, especially when the treatment is not a one-time occurrence. In general, the path of *mussar* and the path of *Chassidus* differ in this: the content of *mussar*, as its name implies, is *mussar* (reproof) in its literal sense—that is, the emphasis is on negative matters and traits, etc. The path of *Chassidus*, however, emphasizes the loftiness and preciousness of the soul (though this requires the negation of all things that prevent the soul’s elevation).

Therefore, it is most appropriate that you set a fixed time for yourself to study the teachings of *Chassidus*. Although I hope that you study it from time to time anyway, that is not a "fixed time" (*kevi'us*). Especially as per the instruction of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, that *kevi'us* means not only in time, but — and this is the main thing — *kevi'us* in the soul. Consequently, you should also adopt this approach in your influence upon your students. For the ways of the Torah are "ways of pleasantness," and there is nothing that can stand before the will. Especially since you have merited (as you put it in your letter) to hear many lofty *sichos* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With respect and a blessing for good tidings regarding all the above.

(From a letter dated Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5718)

## 278

...Regarding what you wrote about an expert physician in Eretz Yisrael who has a good reputation even among the Jewish people, and you ask for my opinion — I did not understand what the doubt is here. In matters of medicine, one does not make such distinctions; "a craftsman does not disparage his craft," as we have seen in actual practice even from our holy *Nesi'im*. Especially since you write that he is a religious man. May the Holy One, blessed be He, send His word and improve his state of health through this person and these treatments.

There is a special *segulah* for these days, as we are approaching the time of the Giving of our Torah, which brings healing to the world, as is explained at length in *Shemos Rabbah* as well, that all of Israel were healthy and whole for the receiving of the Torah...

(From a letter dated 25 Iyar, 5715)

...Regarding what you wrote about your mother-in-law, may she live: there is a well-known rule in such cases that if a physician says "sit and do nothing," one should seek the opinion of another specialist in the field. Therefore, it is worthwhile for your mother-in-law to turn to another specialist. May the Holy One, blessed be He, grant you success in advising her for the best in all details.

(From a letter dated 10 Sivan, 5718)

...Regarding his treatment: he should ask for the opinion of a third specialist physician. If he agrees with one of the aforementioned, he should do so. If he gives a third opinion, he should convey all of this to his family physician and consult with him on how to proceed in practice.

2) Regarding his sister's son, may he live: he should consult with a specialist in this field on how to influence his sister in all the matters you write about.

I will mention the above at the holy gravesite.

(From a response of the Rebbe)

...I cannot understand at all: why does the physician treating your friend not send a description of her condition, etc., to the research institute in Washington? If the reason, as she writes, is that in his opinion they have not found a cure for this there: 1) What will he lose by doing so? 2) How can he know what has been done at the aforementioned institute recently? It is known that it takes several months (and sometimes a year or more) until such institutions publish the results of their research. I see only one reason — a psychological one: not to arouse hope in your friend that, in his opinion, will later lead to disappointment. But there is a solution for this: they can send the description without her knowledge.

(From a letter dated 5 Adar II, 5765)

I received your letter from the 27th of Cheshvan, in which you describe the state of health of your wife, may she live, who, according to the physician's opinion, has several issues and from time to time suffers from gallbladder [problems], etc., and is now bedridden with various pains.

In my opinion, it would be worthwhile to find a general practitioner — meaning, even if he is not so "great," but one who has knowledge of all matters. You should tell him the opinions of all the physicians your wife has visited until now, and ask him to oversee everything and give her general guidance regarding conduct, eating, and drinking. Since our Sages said that healing comes through a certain remedy and a certain person, etc., without limitation as to his greatness or status, it is very possible that precisely a physician of this nature will "hit the mark" for her, and through him, healing will come to your wife.

With a blessing that you report good tidings regarding the improvement of your wife's health.

(From a letter dated 3 Kislev, 5712)

It is understood that if the matter will lead to anger or resentment from one of them, you should suffice with presenting the opinions of the two physicians to their family physician and consult with him...

(From a letter dated 29 Sivan, 5716)

...What you wrote at the end of your letter about whether to turn to a physician who is more of a specialist than Dr. [Name]... and the fear is that perhaps he will have a different opinion and then how to decide.

This fear is sufficient for its time, since in any case, you will not have left the realm of doubt, and the decision in such cases is either the feeling of the person asking himself — as the *Shulchan Aruch* rules that in matters such as these, "the heart knows its own bitterness" — or that you present both opinions before a neutral physician. May the Holy One, blessed be He, guide you on the path that is good for you...

(From a letter dated 21 Kislev, 5715)

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention him and his wife, may she live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that just as you wrote the request, so too you will report good tidings regarding this.

Regarding what you wrote about the achievements of physicians in the United States in the science of medicine: in general, the physicians here and in Eretz Yisrael are in close contact and know what is happening with one another. However, sometimes it is especially worthwhile to ask the physician you are visiting about achievements outside of Eretz Yisrael, and especially in the United States, and regarding the saying of our Sages, "a matter that is not upon a person's mind..."

(From a letter dated 3 Shevat, 5721)

It is understood that, in general, the decision regarding this depends on the level of expertise of those advising. Especially in your situation: according to information here, great specialists in heart medicine from abroad also visit Eretz Yisrael, and then they hold a consultation together with the specialists of Eretz Yisrael. It is worthwhile for you to clarify if there is a possibility for such a consultation in the near future, and then ask the physician among your acquaintances to be examined by the aforementioned, so that they will know their instruction. May it be His will that they succeed in their advice for your speedy healing.

(From a letter dated 26 Elul, 5717)

Act according to the unified opinion of two specialist physicians.
And if there is a detail pertaining to the *Shulchan Aruch*, it is understood that there must be the opinion of a Rav.

## ג. התחזקות באמונה ובטחון

## 282

Torah and mitzvos in general, and increasing in them during times of need and pressure in particular—and surely you will act in this regard in a manner befitting your status and situation, and "whoever adds, it is added to him."

You should certainly keep the three daily study portions established for every person by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: 1) Reciting a portion of Tehillim—as divided according to the days of the month—each day after Shacharis. 2) Studying a portion of the weekly parsha with Rashi’s commentary—on Sunday from the beginning of the parsha until the second aliyah, on Monday from the second until the third, and so on. 3) Studying a daily portion of Tanya as it is divided throughout the year. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for improved health, and awaiting good news,
(From a letter, 16 Menachem Av, 5715)

In response to your letter from Erev Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, in which you write of what you heard from the doctor and the impression it left on you and your wife, may she live.

It is surprising that you seem to have forgotten the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the precise wording of our Sages: "The Torah gave permission to the physician to heal." He emphasized that he has permission to *heal*, but not, Heaven forbid, to cause despondency, etc. Especially in our times, when new medical treatments are developed every day and new medicinal substances are discovered, it is contrary to common sense to predict the future in the manner you describe. If only you would be strong in your bitachon in the Creator of the world and its Guide, who oversees each and every person with individual providence; in the near future you will see tangibly that the aforementioned words were false. Although it is understood that one must take some action by way of nature—see also the Kuntres and the Maamar of the Rebbe Rashab on this—and therefore one should also look into a vegetarian diet...

When one strengthens one's bitachon in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, one draws this down into actual, visible, and revealed good.

## 283

With blessings for long and good years—for you and your wife, may they live—and for much nachas from all your children, may they live, in good health.

Certainly for someone like you, who is a man who has seen affliction and the kindness of Hashem in being saved from distress and many hardships, it is superfluous to elaborate that bitachon in Hashem, the Creator of the world and its Guide, is justified—not only regarding the life of the World to Come, but also regarding matters in this world, even though it is physical and material, and its ways are difficult and harsh, as explained also in the Tanya of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe at the end of Chapter 6. Indeed, even according to medical science, the greater the level of bitachon, the greater the person’s vitality, which also influences the state of their physical health and their state of mind, which in turn adds to their success in their actions and efforts.

Therefore, based on all that has been said in accordance with your letter, it is understood—and my hope is strong, founded on the promise of our Sages that whoever is treated well [by Hashem] is granted long days and years—that after some time, you will be able to report that the situation has improved in the areas you wrote about. May it be His will that this improvement continues and increases.

My hope is that after your visit to [the place] for healing the sick, you will visit there for happy matters—a visit of the healthy—and participate in the farbrengens held there from time to time, which bring healing and encouragement to the spirit of the lowly and the hearts of the crushed—those who are lowly and crushed in the war of the inclinations, the war of the soul against the body, and the spirit against the material. All of this comes as a result of the war of the nefesh elokis against the nefesh habahamis.

With respect and blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.
