## ד. להעסיק כח המעשה ולא כח המחשבה

## 286

### D. Engaging the Faculty of Action, Not the Faculty of Thought

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Elul, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein—which I will read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in which you write regarding the state of your health: I have already written to several people who have asked about such matters that, while on the one hand, one must follow the instructions of doctors—as is explained in many places and cited as a halachic ruling in the *Shulchan Aruch* regarding the laws of Shabbos, *milah*, and so on—on the other hand, this applies only to the actual, practical level. However, the faculty of thought is not a person’s concern at all; one should not dwell on the state of one’s physical health, etc., because this is not one’s profession. That is to say, he is not the doctor for this particular individual, and no benefit will come to the individual from this [dwelling]. Consequently, for him, this falls into the category of thought that has no purpose, and therefore it is a distraction, as it occupies the faculty of thought, preventing it from being invested in what it *should* be thinking about. Anything else is considered as if it were not there. Therefore, regarding himself, he should fulfill the instructions of the doctors in terms of practical action and place his trust in Hashem, that He will send His word and heal him. With blessings for the fulfillment of the requests in the aforementioned *pidyon nefesh*, and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* in particular.
(From a letter dated 3 Elul, 5714)

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 11 Kislev. Regarding what you wrote about the doctors' opinions, it is a great wonder that my words are being distorted, and as a result, the mood is not as it should be. I said, and also wrote, that you should follow the instructions of expert doctors. I also said, and wrote many times, that one should not be *mispa'el* (emotionally affected) by their opinions. As is known, the *Tzemach Tzedek* was precise in saying that a doctor is given permission to heal, and nothing more. Yet, in both of these aforementioned matters, you are doing the opposite: you are not following the instructions of expert doctors, and on the other hand, you *are* becoming *mispa'el* by their opinions. What can I do about this? Surely, one cannot deny a Jewish man or woman their power of free choice. According to what is explained in many places in *Chassidus*, and as is also implied in *Likutei Torah* (Parshas Emor 48b), free choice exists because they are rooted in *Atzmus*, where it is the only place of free choice without any compulsion. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant success to you and your wife, *tichyeh*, that you should follow the instructions in both of these matters, and the outcome will be, as soon as possible, in a revealed and manifest good...
(From a letter dated 17 Kislev, 5715)

...Regarding what you wrote about the state of your health and that you have become despondent over it: surely you know that this is the opposite of our Torah in general, and the teachings of *Chassidus* in particular. The Torah has granted a doctor permission to heal, but at

## 287

the same time, a person must remember and know clearly that the *Ribono shel Olam* is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders. Consequently, one must serve Him, may He be blessed, with joy and a good heart, and trust in the *Ribono shel Olam* to fulfill His promise to provide what the servant needs, as is explained in many places in *Chassidus*. One should not dwell at all on the state of one’s health, or listen to how one is feeling, because these are the doctor’s concerns, not the person’s. To elaborate on such a simple matter is superfluous. May the merit of your involvement in drawing the hearts of the Jewish people to our Father in Heaven stand by you to bring you good news regarding all of the above.
With blessings for success in your holy work, and awaiting good tidings.
(From a letter dated 4 Teves, 5715)

...The sending of the letters was delayed, and in the meantime, your letters from the 15th, 22nd, and 26th of Teves arrived, as well as the telegram. I do not understand why there is panic again regarding your health. I have already said and written to you many times that my opinion on this is clear, and I have also emphasized that, in my opinion, you should completely divert your mind from thoughts about your health, for you are healthy, with the help of Hashem. However, you should fulfill all the doctors' instructions regarding action. I see that even while you were here, you did the opposite in both matters: you dwelled on things that have no basis (without any reason for doing so), and you did not want to keep the schedule of eating and drinking, etc. (also without any logical reason). It seems that even now you are persisting in this behavior. What good will it do for me to write again if you are determined to do the exact opposite? The matter depends only on your own good will...
(From a letter dated 13 Teves, 5716)

...Regarding your own health, I have already said to several of *anash* in such situations that in terms of action, one must fulfill the doctor's instructions, and therefore one must visit him so that he can provide guidance. However, the faculty of contemplation—and even thought—should not be concerned at all with the state of one's health. Especially in your case—there is nothing to overthink. It seems from your letter that you are doing the opposite: you are dwelling on and investing your thoughts in, "What is the state of my health today? Yesterday? Tomorrow and the day after?"—and with strange speculations, at that—and you are not visiting a doctor, and therefore you cannot fulfill his instructions. Since you have already been acting in your own way for many months, perhaps you could try from now on to act according to my suggestion, in both details together?
(From a letter dated 18 Tammuz, 5715)

## 288

The mailing was delayed, and your letter from 26 Shevat was received, as well as the notes from the gathering of...—*tichye*.
Regarding what you wrote in your letter about visiting other doctors: with all due respect, wildness also needs to have a limit. You should ask the doctor—[name]—in a letter. There is no need to run to...—to have him arrange a list of foods and drinks that are better for your health, the approximate times for eating, how many times a day, and the like. Then, fulfill his instructions in practice. For a few weeks, stop your travels from your home to other places, and then you will be able, if you wish, to fulfill the above with greater ease. May it be with success.
(From a letter dated 27 Shevat, 5716)


## ה. תומ"צ ורפואת הנפש מביאים רפואת הגוף

## 296

In response to your letter informing me of your state of health, that you are feeling a depletion of strength and the doctor wishes to perform tests, etc., and you are asking for my opinion—
You may follow his advice and undergo the tests. Regarding the depletion of strength: be careful with *pas shacharis* (breakfast), and from time to time study something—whether in *nigleh* or in *Chassidus*—that you will derive simple enjoyment from. "And it shall be healing to your flesh and marrow to your bones."
When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, for true health.
It is my hope that you will bring me good news in this regard.
It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your health in terms of *ruchniyus*.
Perhaps you have heard the story of one of the people from America who came to ask for the advice of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding his lumber business. After the Rebbe gave him an answer on that, and continued to instruct him in matters of *mitzvos*, the man said that he had not asked about that. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, replied to him: "How strange. Regarding business, where you are the expert and it has no connection to me—you ask for my advice. But regarding *mitzvos*, which are among the fundamental matters and the occupation of my fathers and forefathers—about this you do not ask."
Of course, the cases are not at all comparable—but, in any event, I have more of a connection to the study of *Gemara* and *Chassidus* than to the science of medicine. And if so, how strange!
With blessings for a speedy recovery and true health for you and your wife, may they live.
(From a letter, 29 Shevat, 5711)

At the time, I received the news that your health is not entirely perfect and that you are entering the hospital, in a good and auspicious hour.
You will surely follow the instructions of the expert doctors. It is a known ruling and interpretation of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the Torah grants the doctor permission to heal. The meaning of this "permission" is both authorization and power; for when the Creator of the world gives someone permission to fulfill a good role, since He is the Essence of Good, He certainly desires that the role be fulfilled and therefore also grants him the ability and power to do so.
It is surely unnecessary to urge you to bring those who are with you in the hospital closer to our Father in Heaven through the ways of *ahavas Yisrael*, as our holy *Nesi'im*, may their merit protect us, have instructed us. When one adds to the health of a Jewish person in *ruchniyus*, the Holy One, Blessed be He, adds *middah k'neged middah*—many times over—to the health of the one who exerts himself in this, both in his physical and spiritual health.
With a blessing for true health and for long days and good years, filled with good deeds in Torah and *tzedakah*.
(From a letter, 13 Menachem Av, 5714)

## 297

...Regarding what you wrote about Mr. [Name], may he live: since he has already been to Professor [Name] and was not satisfied with his treatment at the time, and they wish to wait once more for my opinion as to whether he should visit him as I wrote previously, or if I am retracting that—
It is surely unnecessary to inform Mr. [Name] and his wife, may they live, that I am not a professor of medical science, nor even a doctor or a medic. Furthermore, when people ask for my opinion and I write what seems right to me, the person asking is not obligated to carry out what I have said, for the choice is free, and he may act according to his own good will. Consequently, there is no room for any resentment on my part. They should not feel compelled to take any action just to avoid offending my "honor," as it were, for there is no basis for such a concern at all. As for the fact that the treatment of Professor [Name] did not satisfy them at the time, several years have passed since then. I know of many who turned to his assistance and were successful, and I see no reason why it should be different in this case. In any event, however Mr. [Name] and his wife, may they live, decide to act, may the Almighty grant them success so that it will be for the good, both physically and spiritually.
(From a letter, 29 Sivan, 5713)

...Regarding the precision in laying *tefillin* for those who are in need of a blessing, their parents, etc.—
In this, there is a connection that is understood even simply (and according to the conduct that is also understood simply—*middah k'neged middah*). The essence of "schizophrenia" (whatever its cause may be) is a lack of alignment between reality (the environment) as it is, and how the patient "sees" and perceives it in his mind. Consequently: 1) Emotions that correspond to this mental state, such as fear—the fear that people want to harm him, etc. 2) From time to time, changes occur, even to the opposite extreme: from fear that has no basis in reality to an unfounded sense of spiritual exaltation, etc.—a splitting of the soul and perspective, etc.
*Tefillin*—part of the *mitzvah* and its *segulah*—is to subjugate the heart (the emotions) and the mind (the intellect) to the true G-d, of Whom it is said, "I, Hashem, have not changed." Consequently, this brings about alignment between the intellect, the emotions, and reality, etc.
(From a response of the Rebbe)

...7) Regarding what you wrote about his breathing: it is highly probable that this is a matter related to the nerves. When he recites *Krias Shema* upon retiring, together with the general *kavanah* that his focus is on the One who stands over him, as stated in the order of *Krias Shema*—"Hashem is your shadow at your right hand"—it is simple that all undesirable matters have no place at all. This applies to health as well, for "they melt like wax," etc.
8) It is understood that this does not negate the way of nature, i.e., conduct that corresponds to the doctor's instructions, for...

## 299

...Regarding the *avreich*, may he live—
He must be precise regarding the *kashrus* of his food, and in the laying of *tefillin* (that they be checked).
(From a letter, 14 Kislev, 5740)

They should bring him a *Tanya* and he should read it from time to time. Also, a *mezuzah* (checked) in an envelope within an envelope. I will mention him at the *tziyun* for a complete and speedy recovery.
(From a response of the Rebbe)

He should explain to his wife, may she live, that G-d forbid, in such a situation, one should not retract a pledge to *tzedakah*—which is to the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is the Healer of all flesh (and doctors are flesh and blood, but His messengers).
He should travel again to see him and his wife, separately and also together, and explain as above.
I will mention him at the *tziyun*.
(From a response of the Rebbe)


## ו. נתוח, וטפול באברים פרטיים

## 305

...and rest, and that he should be a soldier for Hashem as he ought to be, as the Rambam writes in Hilchos Deios, Chapter 4: "Maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem."
(From a letter of 8 Elul, 5711)

In response to your letter—which you dated 10 Sivan but was only received today—in which you write regarding the state of your health and that several doctors have advised you to undergo surgery for the hernia from which you have been suffering for several years:
In my opinion, since this is the advice of experts in this field, it is the correct course of action. However, it is advisable to have it done after the summer days, not during the hot weather.
May Hashem lead you on the straight path and merit you to instill in your students a spirit of yiras shamayim and to illuminate them with the "candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah," as they are illuminated in the teachings of Chassidus. May the merit of your ancestors assist you, and may all this also serve as an additional channel and vessel for the drawing down and reception of an increase in Hashem’s blessings in all that you require.
(From a letter of 13 Menachem Av, 5712)

In response to your letter of 28 Tishrei, with the pidyon nefesh that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory:
You write regarding the hernia, and that for some time you have felt pain, and even after treatment it did not pass completely.
It is known in such cases that the belt provided for a hernia must be adjusted from time to time to accommodate changes in the body—if one becomes a bit heavier or the opposite, and the like. It is likely that the pain you are experiencing is also due to the belt not fitting properly. Therefore, it is advisable that an expert in this field examine the belt and adjust it as necessary.
(From a letter of 3 MarCheshvan, 5717)

## 310

...one cannot predict the outcome in advance, and one is not always certain that one has taken all the precautions one wishes to take.
As for how to conduct oneself in such cases, one must have a decision on the matter from two doctors who are specialists in this field, in addition to the agreement of a Rav, as mentioned above. May Hashem, blessed be He, lead you in the way that is good for you in all respects.
You surely observe the good custom of Jewish women to give to tzedakah each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.
(From a letter of 24 MarCheshvan, 5723)

...And my hope is that by the time you receive this letter of mine, you have also received news of an improvement in the health of your wife, may she live. Regarding what you wrote about radiation for the head concerning health... I believe I have already written once that this treatment requires extreme caution. There are several treatments that carry no liability, and several treatments that carry, at the very least, less liability, and whose results are known more clearly than the results of radiation treatment.
(From a letter of 18 Shevat, 5716)

Her letter was received, and I have expressed my opinion based on what I have seen in many similar cases: that it is worth trying treatment with compresses, which are effective in softening matters such as those you describe, and often they pass completely. Within a short time, one can already see results if the treatment is appropriate. Surely the doctor will also agree to the above, and you should decide in accordance with the results of the aforementioned.
May Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, send His word and heal her through such-and-such treatment and such-and-such person.
(From a letter of 5 Teves, 5722)

## 311

In response to your letter of 20 Tammuz, in which you write regarding the health of your daughter, may she live, and the opinion of the doctors in this matter: several of them are advising surgery on her hand. It is not clear from your letter whether this is the opinion of a single doctor or many doctors. Furthermore, and most importantly: is this opinion based solely on a lack of knowledge regarding the cause of the ailment (which seemingly is implied, since they have performed various other treatments), or do they know the ailment clearly and these treatments are indeed relevant to the ailment, but in this case, they were unsuccessful? You will surely clarify the above, and in accordance with the information, you will decide.
Furthermore, in such surgeries, there is a type that concerns not so much the surgery itself—which in its style is minor—but the extreme caution required not to touch the nerves and arteries that affect the movement of the finger or fingers. It is also appropriate to clarify the part that is added due to "psychology"—i.e., a matter that is not in the physicality of the finger and hand, but in the power of thought and imagination—that it seems to your daughter that when she returns to work, the pain returns (in which case, her contemplation of the matter of Hashgacha Pratis, and that the One who supervises everyone is also the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, and it is said, "In all your ways [know Him]"—with the emphasis on "all," even the slightest—there is room to say that this will weaken the imagination and the pain). May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the above.
I have a strong hope that you have spent these weeks spreading the wellsprings wherever your hand can reach, and you will surely fulfill this further at the next opportunity.
With blessings for good news in all the above.
(From a letter of 25 Tammuz, 5721)

Regarding what you wrote about your health and that the doctors attribute it to a nerve in the vertebrae of the neck: you are surely aware that there is a method in the medical arts (even though several doctors dismiss it) whereby through manipulation—by experts in this way—of the vertebrae, they bring about improvement in several matters of this kind. Although I must say that I am not enthusiastic about this method, experience has shown that many times it brings benefit. It is worth trying. I believe the name is: Chiropractic.
It is strange that you do not mention anything about the farbrengens of the month of Kislev in general, and of the bright day of 19 Kislev in particular, for it is the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, as the head contains within it the vitality of all the limbs (the days) and draws vitality to them in their respective places.
And to conclude your letter regarding the situation of your daughter—
May Hashem fill the days of her pregnancy properly and easily, and may she give birth to a healthy child at its proper time, properly and easily.
Waiting for good news in all the above.
(From a letter of 11 Teves, 5718)

## 312

In response to your letter of the bright day of 18 Elul, the day on which the two great luminaries were born—the birthday of our teacher the Baal Shem Tov and the birthday of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe.
You write at the request of parents regarding their son, may he live, who stopped speaking. After several treatments that did not help, they performed a treatment on the bones of the neck and an improvement is visible. They ask whether to continue with this, etc.
As it appears from the few words you write about the treatment, this is a method that several doctors have begun to use recently, and they call it Chiropractic—i.e., that there is no mystical matter, etc., involved, even according to them, and also according to those who disagree with them. The difference of opinion is only regarding the extent of the benefit of the matter, and nothing more. In this, seemingly, there is an answer to the question of whether it is permitted to go to the one who treats this.
Nevertheless, it is not my place to issue halachic rulings, especially in the absence of several details. Therefore, they should turn to a Rav who is a teacher of instruction in their vicinity after the details regarding the treatment are known to him.
Regarding the matter itself, if it is permitted and if it is worth going again: since they see an improvement, it is worth continuing with it.
When you provide the name of the son together with his mother's name, I will mention him at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for what he requires. May it be His will that just as you brought the request, you will bring good news in this.
You will surely find appropriate words to explain to the boy's parents that they must increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos. Even if the situation is good in this regard, there is always room to add more, since they are connected to the Holy One, blessed be He, who is infinite, and through this, an increase is added in Hashem's blessings in what is needed for a person and his household.
With blessings for good news and a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*.
(From a letter of 28 Elul, 5719)

...Regarding what you wrote about the trip to Teveria and the positive and negative sides of it.
After asking for her forgiveness, it is like a merchant calculating if he should open a business: he must invest in renting the premises and buying the merchandise a hundred *zuz*, and if he does not open it, there is no place to earn a hundred times a hundred *zuz*. For in our world, there is no matter that does not require investment, whether of spiritual strengths, physical strengths, or money, and this is the ability to earn many times over. Such a calculation applies also to the trip—i.e., the pleasantness involved in the trip to the hot springs of Teveria compared to earning many times over and for long, good days and years that will come through this trip. I wish she had traveled last year, but one does not cry over the past, and I mention this only

## 313

as proof that this trip is not only permitted and outweighs the negative sides she mentions, but is also desirable, and even for the benefit of those who perhaps for a short while will suffer because of this trip.
With blessings for good news and a healthy winter in all respects.
(From a letter of 14 Teves, 5718)

...Regarding what you wrote about the health of your wife, may she live, concerning the habits for which some doctors advise surgery—it is strange that you do not mention if they have tried other methods, such as wearing stockings, massage, injections, etc.—which it is understood that before deciding regarding surgery, they should try these methods. And if they have already exhausted all the above and there is no benefit, then they should hold a consultation (consilium) of two doctors who are experts in the field and act according to their instruction. The Torah has given permission to the doctor to heal. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the above.
Your wife, may she live, surely follows the good custom of the kosher daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. It would be appropriate to check the mezuzos in their home. And you surely keep the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul, as established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Chummash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is known—and at the very least, you should keep them from now on.
With blessings.
(From a letter of 17 MarCheshvan, 5717)

...Regarding what you wrote about the tendons of the legs of your wife, may she live—it is strange that you do not mention if the doctor ordered her to wear rubber stockings, and also that she should interrupt her walking or standing frequently and lie down to rest for a few moments.
May Hashem fill the days of your wife's pregnancy properly and easily, and may she give birth to a healthy child at its proper time, properly and easily.
(From a letter of 8 Tammuz, 5717)

## 314

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of 3 Matos-Masei, in which you write regarding your health and ask for my opinion, as there is a doctor who says it is advisable to perform surgery:
In general, regarding ulcer matters, they are mostly healed by keeping a diet and resting the mind and body, which is understood to be a more correct path than through surgery, etc. But since you write in your letter that this has happened several times that you bled, G-d forbid, etc., and consequently it seems that this is already an old matter for you and it is difficult for you to maintain the necessary care in matters of eating and drinking, etc., therefore, in my opinion, you should consult with two doctors who are experts in this field in particular and act according to their instruction. As for traveling to Rochester for this purpose, I do not know the necessity, since in Chicago there are experts in this, and why should you have the burden of travel, additional expenses, etc.? May Hashem give the doctors whom you consult the correct opinion, through which the verdict of the Torah—that it has given permission (which also means power) to the doctor to heal—will be brought from potential into action (see Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 19, page 40b, for the exact phrasing of "from potential into action"). May Hashem merit you to bring good news regarding the improvement of your health, and that you are adding strength and might to influence your congregation and your surroundings to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven through strengthening the three pillars of Torah, Avodah, and Gemilas Chasadim, illuminated by the light of Torah—this is the teachings of Chassidus.
Enclosed is the Kuntres and the Reshima that were published in connection with the days of redemption and virtue, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which have passed, and which in truth are relevant all year round. It would be appropriate that you use your stay in the hospital to merit your neighbors who are there as well. We do not know what may be, and perhaps this is the purpose and the essence of why they brought you to the hospital. When you complete this mission well, the treatment will naturally follow the essence, etc.
With blessings for a speedy recovery.
(From a letter of 24 Tammuz, 5712)

After a long break, your letter of the third day, on which "it was good" was doubled, was received, in which you write regarding your health and the different opinions of the doctors in this.
In general, it is not understood, for it is well-known in the country that in ulcer matters, a diet is effective if one keeps it precisely. The benefit is not only in calming the pain but also in healing the ulcer. The pills that are added to this are to speed up the healing, strengthen the health, and fill the deficiency in vitamins and the like because of the diet.
Since your letter does not imply all this, perhaps it is worth clarifying and speaking once more with the doctor treating you.
A person must act in the way of nature, and Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, will send His word and heal him through such-and-such person and such-and-such treatment.
(From a letter of 15 Teves, 5722)

## 315

...1) Regarding the cataract surgery that the doctors are urging to perform: you write "the doctors" in the plural, so surely at least two experts are included. Consequently, there is nothing to ponder about this—to overthink—because such surgeries have already become a very common matter, and the caution required in this is well known. From this, it is also understood that, seemingly, traveling to another country for this is not worthwhile for several reasons. As for which doctor to choose, there is a story I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: at the bris milah of one of the grandchildren of the Tzemach Tzedek, which took place during the Tzemach Tzedek's lifetime, they asked the Tzemach Tzedek which mohel to choose—one who is advanced in years and knows the *kavanos*, etc., or a young one who is very simple. The Tzemach Tzedek answered that they should take the young one, because the essence is the *b'po'al mamash* (the actual performance). May Hashem send His word and heal him through such-and-such person, a complete and speedy recovery.
(From a letter of 5 Iyar, 5713)

(From a letter of 23 Teves, 5712)

## 317

In response to your letter of the first day, in which you write regarding your health and especially regarding your eyes.
As you describe the ailment, it seems to be what is called glaucoma. In such cases, it is common to perform surgery even a second time, although, of course, one needs the instruction of the most expert doctor in the field specifically. There are several of this type in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and you should ask them. The Torah has given permission to the doctor to heal.
One of the remedies known in such cases according to our Sages of blessed memory for the light of a person's eyes is caution in Kiddush and Havdalah over wine.
(From a letter of 17 Menachem Av, 5717)

In response to your letter of 2 MarCheshvan, in which you write regarding the health of your daughter, may she live, concerning her eyes and the opinion of the doctors.
First of all, before you decide regarding a trip, the custom in such cases is that the doctor treating her describes what is known to him of her condition and the treatments, and they send this to the doctor whom they wish to visit—in this case, the doctor in Boston. It is also heard here that many from the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, consult with expert doctors in Switzerland. It is appropriate to do the above also regarding them, as surely one can find several contacts in Switzerland through your acquaintances in the Holy Land.
The matter itself as you describe it in your letter is not quite understood, because the level of pressure in the eyes is easily determined, so it is puzzling how there can be doubt in the matter. Furthermore, if the ailment occurred suddenly, there is room to say that it is connected to shock (psychological trauma), and it is not mentioned in your letter at all if they investigated this. For this, there are special treatments. Although this is a simple concern, I found it necessary to also raise this.
At an auspicious time, mention her at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the above.
(From a letter of 9 MarCheshvan, 5717)

...The ear ailment you write about—as you describe it, sometimes this comes from eczema in the ear and a perforation that occurs because of it. If so, there are doctors who treat this and heal it with ointment

and by preventing water from entering the ear. It is understood that the doctor treating her must decide finally regarding this.

...On this occasion, I am interested to know if there is substance to the news that reached me that a doctor... of Cornell University discovered the cause of the skin disease psoriasis: that it comes from an allergy to taurine that is inherited, and therefore the treatment for the aforementioned disease is to reduce the amount of taurine of the patient by reducing the eating of foods containing taurine, mainly meat and fish.

and according to the advice of your friends, etc., this is not the way, of course, in natural reason, and also not according to the instruction of our Torah, which has given permission to the doctor to heal. In response to your letter of 25 Iyar and the one preceding it.
At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for true health. The doctor you consulted surely explained to you that the matter of blood pressure depends to a significant extent on a person's mood. How wonderful are the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Tanya, Chapter 49 (page 70b, end of column 2), "And you chose us," etc., "it is the body," etc. These days are especially suitable for the above, as they are days of preparation for receiving the Torah, when, as our Sages of blessed memory say, all of Israel became healthy in their bodies and sound. (According to all the above, it is understood that there is no need to apologize at all for what you wrote to me regarding this matter, for in addition to the well-known Chassidic saying, "Another's physicality is for me spirituality," the Jewish body is holy, as is understood also from the aforementioned Tanya).

(From a letter of 27 Iyar, 5716)

## 320

...Regarding what you wrote about the rash—the doubt in my words is not understood. Sometimes it happens that certain types of food cause various symptoms in a person, such as a rash and the like. By avoiding these types, the symptoms pass. The difficulty in the matter is to clarify which are the types of food that cause it. The simple (but long) way in this is to avoid a special type of food for some time and see the results.
(From a letter of 21 Adar Sheni, 5717)

...And especially what you write about your son... may he live, it is strange to me because recently they have found several remedies for the disease of epilepsy—G-d forbid—which, although they heal slowly, nevertheless, the improvement is noticeable in the near future and goes on increasing. Therefore, she should speak once more with the expert doctor, who surely knows of the doctors and remedies that have been discovered in recent years for this, so that he will try once more. May Hashem, blessed be He, give him the correct idea how to heal your son, may he live.
Waiting for good news.
(From a letter of 2 Adar, 5715)

Regarding what you wrote about... may he live, in such cases there are remedies that act not only to alleviate but also to increase the interval between one time and another, and the increase goes on growing. With blessings.
(From a letter of Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5718)

At an auspicious time, I will mention your son... may he live, and also those you write about, at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.
Stuttering in speech at this age often comes from sudden fear, and the like. When one clarifies

## 321

the cause, then it is easier to fix the situation until he is completely healed. Therefore, it is appropriate that you consult with a doctor who is an expert in this field.
It is surely superfluous to remind you that as you increase in matters of Torah and its mitzvos, there will be an increase in improvement in all matters, and in the above in particular.
You surely educate your son in a kindergarten (and will continue his education in school) on the purity of holiness.
(From a letter of 11 Menachem Av, 5717)

...And to your writing regarding the stuttering—since a person must do what depends on him in the way of nature, ask and act according to the opinion of a doctor.
But the main thing is that you must increase in perseverance and diligence in the study of Torah, revealed and Chassidus. The study should be as our Sages of blessed memory instructed, "leads to action"—the fulfillment of mitzvos with beauty. In addition to the essence that this is the command of the Holy One, blessed be He, this is also the way to receive the blessing of Him who is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders, and the flesh-and-blood doctor is His messenger.
One sees tangibly that regarding stuttering, strengthening the attribute of trust in Hashem, blessed be He, who supervises everyone with Divine Providence, is especially helpful, since an important cause of the aforementioned ailment is a lack of peace of mind and self-confidence as much as is required.
(From a letter of 25 Tammuz, 5726)

In response to your letter of the tenth of Menachem Av, in which you write that sometimes you feel as if it is becoming tight for you in the windpipe, etc.
This is nothing but a matter connected to the nerves, from which it is understood that if you divert your attention from this and strengthen your trust in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, who gives the Torah and the mitzvah, improvement will occur automatically. However, you must also have some hold in the way of nature by asking a doctor and fulfilling his instruction. It is simple that you must increase in perseverance and diligence in the revealed Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus, and influence your friends in this as well, and it will be good for you physically and spiritually.
With blessings.
(From a letter of 15 Menachem Av, 5717)

## 322

...Regarding what you wrote about a boil—often this comes from the excitement of the nerves and the nature of the food. A small correction in both points brings about a change for the better immediately. Consult also in this with the doctor whose advice you sought.
(From a letter of 9 Teves, 5718)

...And regarding what you wrote about your son... may he live, how his sleep is very light and he wakes up almost every night, etc.
There is room to say that he is lacking something in his nutrition, and when they fill the deficiency, his nerves will surely be strengthened to sleep more restfully. However, you must also check the mezuzah in his room where he sleeps, and also be precise in the kashrus of the food and drink that you give him. Through all this, his situation will go on improving.
Since Divine Providence has placed you in the beautiful portion of educating the children of Israel in education on the purity of holiness, any increase on your part in this work, the work of Heaven, will increase many times over in Hashem's blessings in the private matters of yours and your wife's, may they live. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the above.
(From a letter of 15 Tammuz, 5718)

...Regarding what you wrote about your weakness, and also about disturbances during sleep, there is room to say that both matters are from the lack of order and the lack of fixed times for eating, drinking, sleeping, etc. It is known how much our Rebbes demanded, and also were precise and strict, about a lifestyle of order, and they explained and clarified that the lack of order prevents success in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, especially in such a case that concerns your work in holiness, the work of Zevulun that preceded Yissachar. The manner of your work is explicitly stated in the verse, "Rejoice, Zevulun, in your going out," and so on.
It is appropriate that you ask for the opinion of a doctor in order to calm you from the excitement of the above, and ask him to set for you times for eating, drinking, etc., and as much as possible, try to keep them. May Hashem send His word and heal you and strengthen you.
(From a letter of 14 Sivan, 5718)

## 323

In response to your letter of the fifth day, in which you write regarding the disturbances you have in sleep, etc., and you asked for the opinion of a doctor and for the time being it did not help you.
First of all, you must check the mezuzos in your home and also your tefillin so that they are kosher according to the law. Every weekday before the morning prayer, set aside a few coins for tzedakah, and after the prayer every day, even on Shabbos and Yom Tov, say the monthly Tehillim *shiur*—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month. It is best that not only during the day should you wear a tallis katan checked for its tzitzis, but also sleep in a tallis katan, as the Arizal says in this (brought by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in his Siddur, Laws of Tzitzis). Then my hope is strong that your matters will be arranged.
However, since for everything there must be a hold in nature, and the doctor will surely give you some pills and the like, take them according to the doctor's instruction, but divert your attention completely from the matter of the aforementioned disturbances, and then, as above, slowly over a period of time that is not long, you will return to your strength like any other person. As much as you divert your attention more and increase in your trust in Hashem, the Creator of the world and its Guide, you will be added to in Hashem's blessings and your success in the above and in all your matters.
With blessings for good news in all the above.
(From a letter of 5 Iyar, 5719)

As is well-known, they advise: rest from the aforementioned as much as possible, divert their attention from the aforementioned (and it goes without saying not to exaggerate it).
Less drinking close to sleep, etc.
(From a response, Summer 5783)

## ז. סמי מרפא, זריקות וכו'

## 328

### 7. Medicinal Drugs, Injections, etc.

...I hope that by the time you receive this letter, the health of your entire family, and your own health in particular, has improved. Regarding the migraines you suffer from, in addition to the medicinal drugs that have become more numerous in recent times—including various types—it would be worthwhile for you to obtain a small mezuzah that has been checked and is kosher. Wrap it by itself in a cloth a few times and carry it with you (naturally, only when it is permitted to carry, unlike on Shabbos in a public domain). This will surely influence your health for the better. May Hashem grant you success, so that together with your husband, you may always bring good news for all time.
(From a letter dated 18 Teves, 5715)

I am responding to your letter in which you write about your health and the health of the children, may they live. I hope that by the time you receive this letter, things are already much better.

Regarding what you write about suffering from headaches: you do not mention the diagnosis of the doctors. In such cases, one is usually given pills (tablets) that are called [name of medication]. It might be worthwhile to ask the doctor specifically about this; perhaps he will prescribe them.

In any case, the stronger your *bitachon* in Hashem, who is the *Rofeh Kol Basar U’mafli La’asos* (Healer of all flesh and performs wonders), the faster and better your health will be—especially for those who have seen the *chasadim* of Hashem revealed many times. Hashem will surely continue His *chasadim* and you will be successful in the future as well.

## 329

With blessings for good news.
(From a letter dated 14 Menachem Av, 5718)

In response to your letter, in which you write about your state of health, the headaches, and also regarding the swelling in the neck area.

It is understood that you must seek the opinion of a specialist doctor in the field once again and act according to his instructions.

Regarding what you wrote about the headaches: it may be said that this comes because your cycle is not regular. Once it is regulated through appropriate treatment, the pain will also, at the very least, be lighter.
(From a letter dated 12 Nissan, 5719)

In response to your letter from 19 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding your aunt, may she live.

As you describe her condition, there is room to say that the heart is fine, and the ailment stems from the changes of this age (a decrease in the cycle, its cessation, etc.). It would be worthwhile to prompt her or ask the doctor she visits about this. If this is indeed the case, there are special, mild treatments that alleviate the situation significantly. The main thing is that once she knows the cause of the ailment, it will calm her spirit, and that in itself is a significant matter.

At a time of *ratzon*, I will mention her, as well as her daughter, may she live, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

You surely know of the good custom of the daughters of Israel to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. In any event, she should do so from now on.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.
(From a letter dated 1 Elul, 5717)

## 330

In response to your letter from 4 Tammuz, in which you write about your physical health (it might be worthwhile to suggest to your doctor that some people use a new medication in such cases called Hydrocortisone or similar, although, of course, no two cases are alike, and it is only for the doctor to decide if it is appropriate in this case as well).

As you requested, I will mention you at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a *refuah kerovah* and a *refuah sheleimah*.

Since the physical is connected to the spiritual, in matters such as these, one must increase in *dibbur* of *mitzvah*—that is, in the letters of Torah and *tefillah*—and be more precise in guarding against forbidden speech, and even against repulsive speech or idle chatter, as the distinctions are enumerated in the commentary of the Rambam on the Mishnah, *Avos*, end of Chapter 1.

May the merit of your involvement among the Chabad youth, drawing the hearts of *Bnei Yisrael* to our Father in Heaven, stand by you to bring good news soon regarding all that was mentioned above.

With blessings.
(From a letter dated 10 Tammuz, 5715)

In response to your letter from 28 Shevat, in which you write about the apprehension regarding the new medication, Meticorten—and that there are still doubts as to whether to use it.

In my opinion, you should ask the doctor's opinion regarding the well-known medications, Hydrocortisone, which are of the Cortisone family, but are better; therefore, the doubts regarding their use are fewer. In known cases, they have been using this here for several months, although I do not know if this applies to your wife's treatment...
(From a letter dated 3 Adar, 5716)

Some say to continue as until now with insulin and electricity, etc., and recently, the method of settling for pills and *sichos* is spreading.

May it be the will of the Healer of all flesh, who performs wonders, that He hasten her recovery with the appropriate treatment before her.

With blessings for good news regarding all that was mentioned...

(From a letter dated 17 Sivan, 5719)

...In response to your question: here, in the very recent years, doctors are minimizing shock or insulin treatment, and replacing it with pills (manufactured in Switzerland with some improvements in the USA; the names of the pills vary from country to country and are known to the doctors). They are satisfied with this change, even though the treatment is longer. In any case, the main thing is that in pleasant ways, they should endeavor that he be occupied with work or an activity where he will not feel heavy responsibility.
(From a letter dated 12 Adar, 5722)

I acknowledge receipt of the *pidyon nefesh* for your daughter, may she live. It is strange that it has been a very long time since there was any news from her, and even now you settle for a *pidyon nefesh* and nothing more. Surely you will fill this in on the next occasion. May it be the will that you bring good news.

Regarding what you wrote about your daughter, may she live, mentioned above: as far as one can clarify the situation from your letter, several new treatments have been developed in recent years for such cases, such as pills that accelerate development, etc. It seems that in Switzerland there are great doctors who are experts in this field. It would be worthwhile for you to become informed about this in detail and act according to the information you receive.

I must note regarding the conclusion of your letter, that when Hashem helps and she is healed, you will give, *bli neder*, to *Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*, etc.—this is not a desirable formulation, in the sense of setting conditions with Hashem and stipulating that first He must help and afterwards, etc. The essence of every Jewish person is to do everything possible and to the best of one's ability in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—of which *tzedakah* is a part, and furthermore, it is equal to all the *mitzvos*, to the point that it is called simply "a *mitzvah*" (see *Tanya*, Chapter 37, at length)—and together with this, to pray, ask, and demand from Hashem what one needs in terms of children, life, and abundant sustenance. And this is understood.

With blessings for good news regarding all that was mentioned and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.
(From a letter dated 10 Elul, 5717)

## 333

...with pills that are more effective than [...], and the negative side in them is also less than the aforementioned. Furthermore, in such a manner, there is no need at all to be in a sanitarium. Here, they have recently been using drugs called "Tofranil," and surely you know about them or their equivalents in the Holy Land, may it be built and established.

It is highly probable that a change of location for a few days, such as a visit to the home of friends or the like for a few days, will influence for the good, in a revealed and manifest good.

The surprise is understood that you do not mention the *yom hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*, the tenth of Shevat, and similar activities of his in *hafatzas hamaayanos*. I have already written to several of *Anash* regarding such matters, that if they were to write frequently about the line of "do good"—i.e., *hafatzas hamaayanos* within the strengthening of Judaism in general—this would surely prevent the writing about matters of good that is not attained, especially since the merit of the many assists one.

May it be the will that you bring good news in this as well.
(From a letter dated 17 Shevat, 5721)

Your letter has been received, with your two articles enclosed. As you requested, I looked over the monograph. I must say that your explanation regarding the way to prevent immunity against medicinal drugs is very well received. It is only a wonder how they have not adopted this until now and acted according to this reasoning. Although in the history of the sciences there are many phenomena similar to this, nevertheless, the past should teach the future, and the number of these phenomena should have been decreasing.

It is understood that my intention in this is not to express wonder, but to remark that perhaps they have already researched in the direction you suggest and have also acted upon it, although it is certain that before you printed the article, you researched and inquired into this as much as possible.

Incidentally, although this is not my field, I saw in the tables in your monograph that medications and methods of treatment are brought that were used 150 years ago and more. This is also a wonder, for in any case, over such a long time, they surely used them many times, with changes from the previous methods and improvements in the methods of use. It is impossible that there would not be innovations in this, whether to the right or to the left. The purpose of the table is not the history of the science of medicine, but rather utility regarding medicine and treatment with the medication, in which one should utilize only the most recent results. As the rule in our Torah—to distinguish—which is a logical rule: "The law follows the later authorities," since they saw the words of those who preceded them. It is understood that all of the above is written as the opinion of one for whom this is not his field, and only as a remark from one standing on the outside.


## ח. טפול רפואי בשיטת ה"מדיטצי'"

## 335

### 8. Medical Treatment via the "Meditation" Method

For a long time now, I have been aware of the halachic ruling in Eretz Yisrael regarding the absolute prohibition of various treatments conducted by a "guru," which also include seclusion, contemplation, and the like.

Although the aforementioned ruling—and I believe it is included in its phrasing—is based on the fact that these practices involve elements of avodah zarah, or at the very least, accessories to avodah zarah, which is one of the three categories for which one must sacrifice one's life rather than transgress, nevertheless, the concepts of seclusion and contemplation themselves are not inventions of the aforementioned individuals, nor does their success depend on them, Heaven forbid. The fact that they burn "incense" or similar items is not the essence of the matter, as is obvious and simple.

Therefore, following the style of our Sages, "Should the world be lost because of fools?" I have suggested that it is worthwhile, correct, and perhaps even necessary that you (personally, or at least through those who carry out your wishes) enter into discussions with G-d-fearing physicians who are experts in the fields of neurology, mental health, and psychiatry, and place upon them the obligation (or more accurately, the privilege) to further their studies in treating and healing in this field through seclusion and self-contemplation. Afterward, they should publicize this as much as possible. In addition to the fact that many patients in need of this will be healed, it will also be an effective means to disconnect them from the "gurus" who draw them in with the ropes of the aforementioned treatments, as they will see that the matter can be accomplished without incense, through a G-d-fearing man or woman. Surely, for one of your stature, there is no need for elaboration.
